Prohibition of Sisters, Nieces, and Aunts by Lineage
Ruling on prohibition of sister, nieces, and aunts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which female relatives are permanently prohibited by lineage (qarabah) and cite the Quranic proof for each.

Core Idea
All sisters, nieces, and aunts by blood are permanently prohibited—the Quranic term is general.

This lesson continues the enumeration of permanently prohibited women in marriage. Building on the previous lesson on mothers and daughters, we now cover sisters, nieces, and aunts. The Quranic verses are explicit, and the Hanafi position is that the general term covers all types, whether full or half siblings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited relatives
List the female relatives mentioned: sister, brother's daughter, sister's daughter, paternal aunt, maternal aunt, and their extensions (great-aunts).
The passage uses general terms like 'sister' and 'aunt' without restriction.
2
Cite the Quranic proof for each
For sisters and nieces, the proof is from Quran 4:23. For aunts, the proof is derived from the same verse by analogy or from the general permission of Quran 4:24 for those not specified.
The verse explicitly mentions 'your sisters' and 'daughters of the brother and daughters of the sister'.
3
Explain the principle of generality (umum)
The terms are 'amm (general), covering all types regardless of which parent the relation comes from.
Hanafi usul: al-amm yufidu al-umum (the general term indicates generality).
4
Distinguish which aunts are prohibited and which are not
Paternal and maternal aunts are prohibited, including the sister of one's grandfather/grandmother. However, more distant aunts like the maternal aunt of the father are not prohibited and remain permissible.
The passage explicitly excludes 'ammat ummin wa khalat ab' (paternal aunt of mother, maternal aunt of father).
5
Conclude with the principle of general prohibition
Only those specified by text or consensus are prohibited; all others are permissible based on Quran 4:24.
This is a key Hanafi principle in determining mahram relations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ع) وبنت أخيه: لقوله تعالى: وَبَنَاتُ الْأَخِ وَبَنَاتُ الْأُخْتِ ﴾ (النساء:۲۳) سواء كن هذه الثلاث من الأبوين أو من الأب أو من الأم؛ لأن جهة الاسم عام. And even if they are far, i.e. it also prohibited to marry his sister; due to His statement: 'and your sisters' (4:23). (A) And his brother's daughter: due to His statement: 'and the daughters of the brother and the daughters of the sister' (4:23), whether these three are from both parents, or from the father, or from the mother; because the scope of the term is general. (A, Mis) And his paternal aunt and his maternal aunt [i.e. it is also prohibited to marry his paternal aunt from both parents or from one of them. Commentary
This passage continues the list of women prohibited by lineage (qarabah). It covers sisters (full, consanguine, uterine), brother's daughters, sister's daughters, paternal aunts, and maternal aunts. The proof for sisters is from Quran 4:23 ('and your sisters'). For brother's daughters and sister's daughters, the proof is from Quran 4:23 (وَبنات الأخِ وبنات الأخت). The commentary clarifies that these relatives are prohibited whether they are from both parents, only the father, or only the mother, because the terms are general ('amm). The prohibition extends to certain further relatives like the sister of one's grandfather/grandmother (i.e., great-aunts), but not to all distant maternal and paternal aunts; for example, the maternal uncle's wife is not prohibited. The general principle is that only those specified by text or consensus are prohibited, while others remain permissible (referring to Quran 4:24).

Key Terms
أخت (ukht): Sister; includes full, paternal half, and maternal half sisters.
عمة ('ammah): Paternal aunt; sister of one's father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Prohibition of In-Laws: Musaharah
Explains prohibition of in-laws with conditions and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of permanently prohibited in-law relatives and explain the condition for step-daughter prohibition.

Core Idea
The mother of your wife is haram immediately; her daughter only after consummation.

Marriage creates permanent prohibitions with certain relatives of your spouse. This lesson examines the four Quranically-grounded in-law prohibitions. Understanding the conditions—especially the requirement of consummation for the step-daughter—prevents common errors in application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited categories
Spot the four in-law relationships mentioned: mother of wife, wife's daughter (step-daughter), wife of father (step-mother), and wife of son (daughter-in-law).
The text uses 'امرأته' for wife, and 'أبيه' for father, 'ابنه' for son.
2
Note the condition for step-daughter
The phrase 'إن دخل بها' (if he consummated with her) indicates that step-daughter prohibition is conditional on consummation with the wife.
No consummation? The step-daughter remains halal.
3
Recognize the absolute prohibitions
For mother-in-law, step-mother, and daughter-in-law, no condition is mentioned; they are haram upon the marriage contract itself.
This includes cases where the father/son never consummated.
4
Apply the extension to ascendants/descendants
The text 'وإن بعدتا' extends the prohibition to grandfathers and grandsons: wife of your grandfather (even high) and wife of your grandson (even low) are haram.
Qiyas based on the original categories.
5
Connect proofs to rulings
Each prohibition is supported by a specific Quranic verse (4:23,4:22). Note the wording and how it determines the ruling.
E.g., 'حلائل أبنائكم' explicitly mentions 'from your loins' to exclude adopted sons.

(ع)] وتدخل في الحرمة عمة جده وجدته وخالتهما للأبوين أو لأب وأم وأما عمة عمة أمه وخالة خالة أبيه فحلال كبنت وخاله وخالته؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُحِلَّ لَكُمْ مَا وَرَاءَ ذَلِكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٢٤) (فتح) وامرأة أبيه: [مطلقاً ودخل بها أو لم يدخل. (مسكين)] لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَنْكِحُوا مَا نَكَحَ آبَاؤُكُمْ ﴾ (النساء:۲۲) فيتناول منكوحته وطيا وعقدا صحيحا، وكذلك لفظ الآباء يتناول الآباء والأجداد سواء دخل الأب بها أو لم يدخل، وقوله: "ابنه" أي وامرأة ابنه لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَلَائِلُ أَبْنَائِكُمُ الَّذِينَ مِنْ أَصْلَابِكُمْ﴾ (النساء:۲۳) سواء دخل بها أو لم يدخل، وذكر الأصلاب لإسقاط اعتبار التبني؛ لأن التبني نسخ بقوله تعالى: ادْعُوهُمْ لِآبَائِهِمْ ﴾ (الأحزاب:٥) (فتح) وابنه: أي امرأة ابنه؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَلائِلُ أَبْنَائِكُمْ (النساء: ۲۳). ( مص) وإن بعدتا: أي الأب والابن كامرأة الجد وإن علا، والمرأة ابن ابنه وإن سفل. (ط، ع)
And the mother of his wife and his daughter if he has consummated the marriage, and the wife of his father and his son. ... And the wife of his father: [absolutely, whether he consummated or not.] due to His statement: 'And do not marry what your fathers married' (4:22) so it includes his woman by intercourse and valid contract, and likewise the word 'fathers' includes fathers and grandfathers whether the father consummated or not. And his statement: 'his son' meaning the wife of his son, due to His statement: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (4:23), whether he consummated or not, and mentioning 'loins' is to negate consideration of adoption, because adoption was abrogated by His statement: 'Call them to their fathers' (33:5). And his son: meaning the wife of his son; due to His statement: 'And the wives of your sons' (4:23). And even if they are distant: meaning the father and son like the wife of the grandfather even if high, and the wife of the son's son even if low.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationships (musaharah). It covers four categories: (1) the mother of one's wife becomes prohibited immediately upon the marriage contract, regardless of consummation—this is the Hanafi view, contrary to some who require consummation for prohibition. (2) The step-daughter (rabibah) is prohibited only if the husband has consummated the marriage with her mother; if he divorces before consummation, she is halal. (3) The wife of one's father (step-mother) is absolutely prohibited, whether the father consummated or not, because the verse 'do not marry what your fathers married' includes both intercourse and valid contract. 'Fathers' includes grandfathers. (4) The wife of one's son (daughter-in-law) is absolutely prohibited, with the same ruling. The comment on 'from your loins' excludes adopted sons, as adoption is abrogated. The final phrase 'even if they are distant' extends the prohibition to grandfathers and grandsons in the ascending and descending lines.

Key Terms
المصاهرة (al-musaharah): Relationship by marriage; in-laws. The permanent prohibition of marriage to certain relatives of one's spouse.
الربيبة (al-rabibah): Step-daughter, daughter of one's wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the step-daughter (rabibah) become prohibited for the step-father?
A) Immediately upon the marriage contract with her mother
B) Only if she is in his custody (al-hujur)
C) Only after he consummates the marriage with her mother
D) She is never prohibited if her mother is divorced before consummation

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of in-laws is rooted in Quranic texts: mother-in-law, step-daughter (conditional on consummation), step-mother, and daughter-in-law are permanently haram.

Prohibition by Breastfeeding (Rada')
ruling_with_proof: textual basis and expanded application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that breastfeeding creates the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage and distinguish the Hanafi position on laban al-fahl from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
All relatives prohibited by lineage are equally prohibited by breastfeeding — the milk bond mirrors the blood bond.

This lesson expands our understanding of permanent marital prohibitions (mahram) beyond blood ties. The Hanafi school, based on the Quran and hadith, establishes that breastfeeding creates exactly the same set of prohibited relationships. However, there is a critical difference with the Shafi'i school concerning whether the husband's milk (laban al-fahl) also creates prohibition. We will examine the textual proofs and the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
State the general principle: breastfeeding prohibits marriage to the same relatives as lineage (e.g., mother, daughter, sister, etc.).
This is the foundational concept of rada'.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the Quranic verse (4:23) and prophetic hadith that establish this rule.
The hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' is a key proof.
3
Understand the Expansion
Recognize that all previously listed female relatives (mother, daughter, sister, etc.) are included when related by milk.
The text explicitly lists them.
4
Examine the Ikhtilaf
Note the dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding laban al-fahl (the milk attributed to the husband).
Hanafi: creates prohibition; Shafi'i: does not.
5
Evaluate Practical Consequence
Determine which marriages are allowed/prohibited in each school based on this ikhtilaf.
For example, marrying the daughter of one's milk father is prohibited in Hanafi but allowed in Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكل رضاعاً: [ أي وحرم أيضاً تزوج جميع من ذكرت من المحرمات. (ع)] أي الأم والبنت والأخت وبنات الإخوة والعمة والخالة وأم الزوجة وبنتها وزوجة الأب وزوجة الابن كل ذلك يحرم من الرضاع كما يحرم من النسب؛ لقوله تعالى: هَاتُكُمُ اللَّاتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُمْ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ (النساء:۲۳) ولقوله عليه: "يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب" وفي حليلة الابن من الرضاع، وامرأة الأب من الرضاع خلافا للشافعي بناء على أصله أن لبن الفحل لا يتعلق به التحريم، والحجة عليه ما روينا، ومن أراد ضبط مسائل حرمة الرضاع فليحفظ ما أنشد بعض الأفاضل: از جانب شیرده همه خویش شوند وزجانب شيرخوار زوجان وفروع
And all [the previously mentioned relatives] are [prohibited] through breastfeeding: [i.e., and also prohibited is marrying all that were mentioned of the prohibited women.] meaning the mother, daughter, sister, daughters of brothers, paternal aunt, maternal aunt, mother of wife, daughter of wife, wife of father, wife of son—all of that is prohibited through breastfeeding just as it is prohibited through lineage; due to His statement: 'Your mothers who nursed you and your sisters from breastfeeding' (4:23) and due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'What is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by breastfeeding.' And regarding the wife of a son through breastfeeding and the wife of a father through breastfeeding, there is a difference with al-Shafi'i based on his principle that the milk of the male (father) does not establish prohibition, and the proof against him is what we have narrated. And whoever wants to master the issues of the prohibition of breastfeeding, let him memorize what some virtuous one composed: 'From the side of the nursing woman, all become relatives; from the side of the nursling, spouses and branches.'
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage extends the prohibition of marriage to all previously listed female relatives (mother, sister, aunt, etc.) if they are related through breastfeeding rather than blood. The Quranic verse in al-Nisa' (4:23) explicitly mentions 'your mothers who nursed you and your sisters from breastfeeding.' The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'What is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by breastfeeding.' Thus, nursing establishes the same permanent prohibitions as blood relations. The commentator notes a disagreement with al-Shafi'i regarding the wife of a son from breastfeeding and the wife of a father from breastfeeding; Shafi'i holds that the milk of the male (i.e., the husband's milk, as he is the 'owner of the milk' or الفحل) does not create prohibition, while the Hanafis rely on a hadith that the prohibition extends through the milk of the father as well. The Persian couplet summarizes the rule: from the side of the wet nurse, all her relatives become mahram; from the side of the child nursed, the child's spouse and children are affected.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rada'): Breastfeeding that establishes marital prohibitions.
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): The milk attributed to the male (husband) because the lactation occurs from his milk; i.e., the milk of the wet nurse's husband's child (since the milk is produced due to pregnancy from him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding breastfeeding revolves around:
A) The number of feeds required for prohibition
B) The age of the child at the time of breastfeeding
C) Whether the milk of the husband (laban al-fahl) creates prohibition
D) Whether the wet nurse must be a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Breastfeeding establishes the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage, and according to Hanafi, this includes prohibitions through the milk of the husband (laban al-fahl).

The Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters in Marriage and Intercourse
Ruling with proof: prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage and intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two sisters in marriage and intercourse, distinguish between permissible ownership and prohibited intercourse, and explain the proof and the dispute with Caliph Uthman.

Core Idea
Combining two sisters in intercourse is haram, but ownership alone is permissible.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on combining two sisters in marriage or sexual intercourse under right hand possession. The Quran explicitly prohibits marrying two sisters simultaneously, and the Ḥanafī school extends this to intercourse with owned slave-girls based on a ḥadīth and qiyās. We will also explore a notable disagreement with Caliph Uthman and see how the Ḥanafī proof resolves it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being prohibited? The text states that combining two sisters in marriage or in intercourse by right hand possession is prohibited. Note that ownership alone (without intercourse) is allowed.
The ruling is ḥarām for the combination, not for ownership.
2
Locate the dalīl
The primary proof is Quran 4:23: 'And that you combine between two sisters.' For intercourse under ownership, the Ḥanafī school cites the ḥadīth: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine two sisters.'
The ḥadīth is aḥad but the meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The Quranic verse directly prohibits marrying two sisters. The ḥadīth extends this prohibition to intercourse by analogy, since both involve sexual access to two sisters simultaneously.
The connection is through the common meaning of combining in sexual relations.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Caliph Uthman allowed intercourse with two sisters under right hand possession based on Quran 4:3: 'Or what your right hands possess.' He took the verse as general permission. The majority, including Ali, disagreed.
The dispute is between the generality of the verse and the specific ḥadīth.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The Ḥanafī school adopts the view of Ali and the majority: the ḥadīth qualifies the general verse. Thus, combining in intercourse is ḥarām. This is the muftā bihī position.
The evidence for the Ḥanafī view is stronger due to the specific prophetic prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمع بين الأختين نكاحاً ووطياً بملك يمين، فلو تزوّج أي من حيث الوطء كم أخت أمته الموطوءة لم يطأ واحدة منهما حتى يبيعها، المنكوحة والموطوءة وإن بعدتا: أي الأب والابن كامرأة الجد وإن علا، والمرأة ابن ابنه وإن سفل. (ط، ع) والكل رضاعاً: [ أي وحرم أيضاً تزوج جميع من ذكرت من المحرمات. (ع)] أي الأم والبنت والأخت وبنات الإخوة والعمة والخالة وأم الزوجة وبنتها وزوجة الأب وزوجة الابن كل ذلك يحرم من الرضاع كما يحرم من النسب؛ لقوله تعالى: هَاتُكُمُ اللَّاتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُمْ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ (النساء:۲۳) ولقوله عليه: "يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب" وفي حليلة الابن من الرضاع، وامرأة الأب من الرضاع خلافا للشافعي بناء على أصله أن لبن الفحل لا يتعلق به التحريم، والحجة عليه ما روينا، ومن أراد ضبط مسائل حرمة الرضاع فليحفظ ما أنشد بعض الأفاضل: از جانب شیرده همه خویش شوند وزجانب شيرخوار زوجان وفروع والجمع : بالرفع عطف على قوله: "تزوج أمه" إي حرم الجمع. (ع) نكاحاً: أي من حيث النكاح؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنْ تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ (النساء:۲۳) . (ع) ووطياً بملك يمين: أي يحرم الجمع بين الأختين من حيث الوطء بملك يمين، وبدون الوطء يجوز الجمع وهو قول علي بن أبي طالب الله، وقال عثمان الله يجوز الجمع بينهما وطيا أيضاً؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوْ مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ (النساء: ٣) وعامة العلماء على قول علي الله، ولو قبل إحداهما بشهوة حرم وطي واحدة منهما ودواعيه، حتى يحرم فرج الأخرى بتمليك أو نكاح أو عتق، وعند الثلاثة: لا يحرم الدواعي إلا في قول للشافعي له. [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۹۴/۱] وحرمة الجمع بين الأختين وطيا؛ لقوله عليه: "من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يجمعن أختين". (مستخلص) يمين: قيد به؛ لأنه لا يحرم الجمع ملكاً بدون الوطء. (ط) النكاح، ولكن لا يجوز له الوطء بإحداهما. (ط،ع) ماءه في رحم لم يطأ: أي صح ا حتى يبيعها أي يفعل بها فلا يحرم به وطيها عليه من بيع كل أو بعض أو هبة مع تسليم أو عتق أو كتابة أو تزويج، ولو قال: "حتى يحرمها على نفسه لكان أولى، فإذا فعل بيع أمته أو تزويجها أو طلاق المنكوحة حلل له وطء واحدة منهما، وقال مالك: لا يصح النكاح حتى يحرم الأمة على نفسه؛ لأن المنكوحة موطوءة حكما؛ إذ النكاح ملحق بالوطء في حق النسب، فلو صح النكاح لصار جامعا بينهما وطياً وهو ممتنع، قلنا: نفس العقد ليس بوطء، وإنما يصير وطيا عند ثبوت حكمه وهو حل الوطء، وإنما قيد الأمة بالموطوءة؛ لأنها إن لم تكن موطوءة يطأ المنكوحة قبل بيع الأمة. (مسكين، فتح) يبيعها: أي الموطوءة كي لا يكون جامعا بينهما وطيا حقيقة. (ط،ع)
And combining between two sisters [is prohibited] in marriage and in intercourse by right hand possession. So if one marries [the sister of his slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse], he may not have intercourse with either of them until he sells her—the married woman and the possessed woman. ... And combining: in the nominative, coordinated with his statement: 'he marries his mother' i.e., the combination is prohibited. In marriage: i.e., in terms of marriage; due to His statement: 'And that you combine between two sisters' (4:23). And intercourse by right hand possession: i.e., it is prohibited to combine between two sisters in terms of intercourse under right hand possession, and without intercourse, combining is permissible—this is the statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him). And Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) said that combining between them in intercourse is also permissible, due to the general nature of His statement: 'Or what your right hands possess' (4:3). The general body of scholars follow the statement of Ali. And if he kisses one of them with desire, intercourse with either of them is prohibited and its causes, until the private part of the other is made prohibited by transfer of ownership, marriage, or emancipation. According to the three [imams], it does not prohibit the causes except in a saying of al-Shafi'i. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/194] And the prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse is due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine two sisters.' (Mustakhlas). 'Yamin' is a qualifier; because combining is not prohibited in ownership without intercourse. ... (the text continues with detailed ruling on selling)
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage covers the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage or in sexual intercourse with slave-girls. The Quranic verse (4:23) prohibits marrying two sisters simultaneously. The text extends this to intercourse with two sisters under ownership (slave-girls). There is a disagreement attributed to Caliph Uthman who permitted intercourse with two sisters based on the general permission of 'what your right hands possess', but the majority (including Imam Ali) restrict this. The Hanafi position is that combining them in intercourse is prohibited, but it is permissible to own both sisters without having intercourse with both. If a man kisses one sister with desire, it becomes prohibited to have intercourse with either until he makes the other forbidden to himself by selling, freeing, or marrying her off. Further, if a man has a slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse and then marries her sister, the marriage is valid but he cannot have intercourse with either until he sells the slave-girl (or divorces the wife, etc.). This is the Hanafi ruling, in contrast to Malik who holds the marriage invalid. The proof includes a hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine two sisters.'

Key Terms
الجمع بين الأختين (al-jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): Combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse simultaneously.
وطئ بملك يمين (wat' bi-milk yamin): Sexual intercourse with a slave-girl whom one owns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The marriage is invalid and must be annulled immediately.
B) The marriage is valid, but he cannot have intercourse with either until he sells or frees the slave-girl.
C) He may have intercourse with whichever he wishes.
D) He must divorce the wife and keep the slave-girl.

Key Takeaway
Combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse is haram; ownership alone is permissible, but if intercourse occurs with one, the other becomes prohibited until the first is removed from his possession.

Combining Two Sisters: Ruling, Proofs, and Conditions
Forbids marrying or having intercourse with two sisters concurrently

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two sisters in marriage or intercourse, and identify the conditions that trigger prohibition and how it can be removed.

Core Idea
Combining two sisters in intercourse is haram; ownership without intercourse is permissible.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the prohibition of simultaneously having two sisters as wives or concubines. It clarifies that the prohibition applies to intercourse, not mere ownership, and discusses the effect of preliminaries like kissing with desire. The text also presents intra-Hanafi disagreement and a response to Malik's objection, helping you understand both the ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: combining two sisters (in marriage or as concubines for intercourse) is haram. Note that ownership alone, without intercourse, is permissible.
This follows the view of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, supported by the majority.
2
Analyze the evidence
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine two sisters.' This specifies the general permission in Quran 4:3 ('Or what your right hands possess').
The hadith is ahad but accepted as authoritative here.
3
Examine the effect of kissing with desire
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man kisses one sister with desire, intercourse with both becomes prohibited until he removes the right to one (by sale, marriage, emancipation, etc.).
This is a stricter view compared to the Three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar).
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The Three hold that only actual intercourse triggers the prohibition; preliminaries like kissing do not. The mufta bihi view is Abu Hanifa's.
Al-Shafi'i reportedly has a view similar to Abu Hanifa on this.
5
Review the remedy and Malik's objection
To lift the prohibition, the man must remove his right to one sister—e.g., by selling, emancipating, or marrying her off. Malik argued that marriage itself creates a 'constructive intercourse' that would make combination impossible, but the Hanafi response is that the contract alone is not intercourse.
The text clarifies that the selling referred to is of the one who was actually had intercourse, not the married one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمع بين الأختين نكاحاً ووطياً بملك يمين: أي يحرم الجمع بين الأختين من حيث النكاح ومن حيث الوطء بملك يمين، وبدون الوطء يجوز الجمع وهو قول علي بن أبي طالب، وقال عثمان يجوز الجمع بينهما وطياً أيضاً؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوْ مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٣) وعامة العلماء على قول علي، ولو قبل إحداهما بشهوة حرم وطي واحدة منهما ودواعيه، حتى يحرم فرج الأخرى بتمليك أو نكاح أو عتق، وعند الثلاثة: لا يحرم الدواعي إلا في قول للشافعي له. وحرمة الجمع بين الأختين وطياً؛ لقوله عليه: من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يجمعن أختين. يمين: قيد به؛ لأنه لا يحرم الجمع ملكاً بدون الوطء. النكاح، ولكن لا يجوز له الوطء بإحداهما. حتى يبيعها أي يفعل بها فلا يحرم به وطيها عليه من بيع كل أو بعض أو هبة مع تسليم أو عتق أو كتابة أو تزويج، ولو قال: حتى يحرمها على نفسه لكان أولى، فإذا فعل بيع أمته أو تزويجها أو طلاق المنكوحة حلل له وطء واحدة منهما، وقال مالك: لا يصح النكاح حتى يحرم الأمة على نفسه؛ لأن المنكوحة موطوءة حكماً؛ إذ النكاح ملحق بالوطء في حق النسب، فلو صح النكاح لصار جامعاً بينهما وطياً وهو ممتنع، قلنا: نفس العقد ليس بوطء، وإنما يصير وطياً عند ثبوت حكمه وهو حل الوطء، وإنما قيد الأمة بالموطوءة؛ لأنها إن لم تكن موطوءة يطأ المنكوحة قبل بيع الأمة. يبيعها: أي الموطوءة كي لا يكون جامعا بينهما وطياً حقيقة.
And combining two sisters in marriage and intercourse by right hand possession: i.e., it is prohibited to combine two sisters in marriage and in intercourse by right hand possession. Without intercourse, combination is permissible, and this is the saying of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. 'Uthman said that combination is permissible even with intercourse, due to the generality of His saying: 'Or what your right hands possess' (4:3). The majority of scholars follow 'Ali's saying. And if he kissed one with desire, intercourse with one of them becomes prohibited, and [so do] its preliminaries, until the private part of the other becomes prohibited by transfer of ownership, marriage, or emancipation. According to the Three (scholars), the preliminaries do not cause prohibition, except in one saying of al-Shafi'i. The prohibition of combining two sisters in intercourse is due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine two sisters.' 'Right hand' is a restriction; because combination in ownership without intercourse is not prohibited. [As for] marriage, he is not allowed to have intercourse with one of them. Until he sells her: i.e., does with her [the act] that would not cause prohibition of intercourse with her, such as selling all or part, or giving as a gift with delivery, or emancipation, or kitabah, or marriage. If he sells his slave-girl or marries her or divorces the married one, then he is permitted to have intercourse with one of them. Malik said: The marriage is not valid until he prohibits the slave-girl to himself, because the married woman is effectively considered as having intercourse, since marriage is attached to intercourse in respect of lineage; if the marriage were valid, he would be combining two sisters in intercourse, which is forbidden. We say: The contract itself is not intercourse, it only becomes intercourse when its effect is established, which is the permissibility of intercourse. The slave-girl was restricted to the one who was actually [had] intercourse, because if she was not had intercourse with, he would have intercourse with the married woman before selling the slave-girl. 'Sells her' means the one who was had intercourse with, so that he not be combining two sisters in intercourse literally.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage or as concubines. The Hanafi position, following 'Ali, is that it is prohibited to have two sisters as wives or as concubines for simultaneous intercourse. However, it is permissible to own both without intercourse. If he kisses one with desire, then he cannot have intercourse with either until he removes the prohibition on the other by selling, emancipating, or marrying her off. There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: the 'Three' (probably Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar) hold that the preliminaries do not cause prohibition unless actual intercourse. The text then discusses the condition of selling the slave-girl to remove the prohibition, and a response to Malik's objection.

Key Terms
الجمع بين الأختين (al-jamʿ bayna al-ukhtayn): The act of having two sisters as wives or concubines simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi view), if a man kisses one of his two sister-slave-girls with desire, what is the ruling?
A) He may still have intercourse with the one he kissed.
B) He cannot have intercourse with either until he sells one.
C) The kiss nullifies his ownership of both.
D) Only the sister he did not kiss becomes prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Combining two sisters in intercourse is haram; kissing with desire triggers the same prohibition according to Abu Hanifa's relied-upon view.

8 min
Marrying Two Sisters with Unknown Priority: Separation and Half Mahr
Ruling on separation and mahr distribution for two invalid marriages with unknown order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man marries two sisters in two contracts with unknown priority and apply the rule to the basic case of equal named mahrs before consummation.

Core Idea
When priority of two prohibited marriages is unknown, both are dissolved and the women share the mahr equally if named and equal.

This lesson examines the case where a man contracts marriage with two sisters in separate contracts but cannot recall which was first. Since simultaneous marriage to sisters is prohibited, one contract is necessarily invalid. The Hanafi school provides a clear procedure: the judge dissolves both marriages, and the mahr is distributed equally if the mahrs are identical and named. This ruling balances the rights of both women while respecting the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Two marriages to sisters, unknown which is first → one is invalid but we cannot determine which. This creates a dilemma: the valid wife is entitled to full mahr, the invalid one to nothing if no consummation, but we cannot assign.
The problem arises only if the man does not know which contract preceded.
2
State the court's action
The judge (qadi) separates the man from both women (al-farq). This is wajib because one marriage is certainly invalid and the uncertainty cannot be resolved.
If he knew which was first, only the second would be dissolved.
3
Determine mahr obligation for the basic case
The first (valid) wife is due full mahr; since we do not know who is first, each woman receives half the mahr – but only if: the mahr is named in the contract, the mahrs are equal, and divorce occurred before consummation.
If the women agree to accept half, the judge awards it; otherwise if they merely claim without agreeing, nothing is awarded due to ignorance of the rightful recipient.
4
Note conditions and variations
The basic ruling applies when each claims to be first with no evidence. If mahrs differ, each gets a quarter of her own mahr. If no mahr named, one single mut'ah is due. If separation after consummation, each gets full mahr.
These variations will be explored in the next lesson.
5
Recognize the scope
The rule is not limited to sisters; it applies to any pair of women whose simultaneous marriage is prohibited (e.g., a woman and her mother, aunt and niece). The key is two separate contracts with unknown priority.
If they were in one contract, both are void and no mahr except by intercourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تزوج أختين في عقدين، ولم يدر الأول فرق بينه وبينهما، ولهما نصف المهر، وبين امرأتين أية فرضت ذكراً حرم النكاح أي أية امرأته منهما أي فرق القاضي الرجل الأختين أي الأختين المذكورتين أختين في عقدين [ وكذا كل من لا يحل جمعه من المحارم كامرأة وأمها . (ط) ذكر الأختين ليس بقيد، بل تزوج امرأتين ممن لا يجوز جمعه في نكاح من المحارم كذلك، وقيد بالعقدين؛ لأنهما لو كانا في عقد واحد بطلا، فلا يجب لهما المهر إلا بالوطء، وقوله : فلم يدر احترز به عما إذا درى الأول، فإنه حينئذ يجوز العقد الأول، فيحل وطيها إلا إذا وطئ الثانية فحينئذ تحرم الأولى ما دامت الثانية في العدة، ولا يحل وطئ الثانية لفساد العقد. (عيني، فتح) ولم يدر الأول: أي العقد الأول، ولم يدخل بواحدة منهما. (ط،ع) لا ندري بينه وبينهما: أي بين الرجل وبين الأختين؛ لأن نكاح أحدهما باطل بيقين، ولا وجه للتعيين لعدم الأولوية. (ع) نصف المهر: [ أو مسمي واستوى مهرهما، وادعت كل أنها الأولى ولا بينة لهما. (ط)] لأنه وجب للأولى منهما فيصرف إليهما لعدم الأولوية، هذا إذا ادعت كل واحدة منهما أنها هي الأولى، ولا بينة لهما، أما إذا قالتا: أي النكاحين أول لا يقضى لهما بشيء؛ لأن المقضي له مجهول والجهالة تمنع صحة القضاء إلا أن تتفقا على أخذ نصف المهر فيقضى لهما به، وعن أبي يوسف: لا يجب لهما شيء للجهالة، وعن محمد: يجب المهر كاملاً، ثم هذا إذا كان مهراهما متساويين وهو مسمى في العقد، وكان الطلاق قبل الدخول وإن كانا مختلفين يقضى لكل واحدة منهما بربع مهرها، وإن لم يكن مسمى في العقد تجب متعة واحدة لهما بدل نصف المهر، وإن كانت الفرقة بعد الدخول يجب لكل واحدة منهما المهر كاملاً، وكل ما ذكر من الأحكام بين الأختين فهو الحكم بين كل من لا يجوز جمعه من المحارم رمز الحقائق: ١٩٥/١]
And if he married two sisters in two contracts, and he does not know which is first, the judge separates him from both of them, and they have half the mahr each. And between two women, if one of them were presumed male, marriage would be prohibited... meaning whichever of the two women is his wife. The judge separates the man from the two sisters mentioned, and likewise for any pair that cannot be combined among the mahram, like a woman and her mother. The mention of 'two sisters' is not restrictive; rather, if one marries two women from among those whose combination in marriage is not allowed, the same applies. It is restricted to two contracts because if they were in one contract, both would be void and no mahr would be due except by intercourse. And his saying 'he does not know' excludes the case where he knows which is first, for then the first contract is valid, and it is permissible to have intercourse with her, unless he had intercourse with the second, then the first becomes prohibited as long as the second is in her waiting period, and intercourse with the second is not permissible due to the nullity of the contract. (al-'Ayni, Fath) 'He does not know the first' means the first contract, and he has not had intercourse with either. (T, 'A) 'We do not know between him and them' means between the man and the two sisters, because one of the marriages is definitely invalid, and there is no way to specify due to lack of priority. ('A) 'Half the mahr' [if the mahr is named and equal, and each claims she is the first and there is no evidence for either...] because it is due to the first of them, and it is paid to both due to lack of priority. This applies if each of them claims she is the first and they have no evidence. But if they say 'which of the two marriages was first?' nothing is awarded to them because the recipient is unknown and ignorance prevents a valid judgment, unless they agree to accept half the mahr, then it is awarded to them. According to Abu Yusuf: nothing is due to them due to ignorance. According to Muhammad: the full mahr is due. Then this is if their mahrs are equal and named in the contract, and the divorce occurred before consummation. If they are different, each gets a quarter of her mahr. If there is no named mahr in the contract, one single gift (mut'ah) is due to them instead of half the mahr. If the separation occurred after consummation, each gets the full mahr. All that has been mentioned regarding the rulings between two sisters applies to any pair whose combination is not allowed among the mahram. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 1:195]
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where a man marries two sisters in two separate marriage contracts, and he does not know which contract took place first. Since it is prohibited to be married to two sisters simultaneously, one of the marriages must be invalid. However, since we cannot determine which one, the judge separates him from both. Regarding the mahr, the general rule is that the first wife is entitled to her mahr (since her marriage was valid), but since we cannot identify who is first, the money is divided between them. The text details various scenarios: if the mahr is named and equal, each gets half; if the mahrs are different, each gets a quarter of her own mahr; if the separation was after consummation, each gets full mahr. There is also a difference of opinion among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the obligation of mahr when there is ignorance. The ruling applies not only to sisters but to any two women who cannot be lawfully married together (e.g., a woman and her mother).

Key Terms
الفرق (al-farq): The judge's decree of dissolution between the man and both women.
المهر (al-mahr): The bridal gift (dower) specified in the marriage contract.
المحارم (al-mahrim): Relatives by blood or marriage who are permanently prohibited for marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the basic case (unknown priority, no consummation, equal named mahrs), what does the judge do?
A) The judge separates the man from both women and awards each half the mahr.
B) The judge asks the women to settle and only awards half if they agree.
C) The judge upholds the first marriage and dissolves the second.
D) The judge awards each woman the full mahr because of the uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
When two prohibited marriages occur with unknown order, both are dissolved, and each woman receives half the mahr under the basic conditions, reflecting Abu Hanifa's view.

Variations and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Mahr Distribution
Detailed variations of mahr and ikhtilaf on obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the mahr rules for unequal mahrs, no named mahr, and post-consummation, and explain the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
The mahr varies with circumstances: quarter each for unequal, one mut'ah for unnamed, full each after consummation; ikhtilaf on obligation.

Building on the basic ruling, this lesson explores the variations in mahr when the mahrs are unequal, when no mahr is named, and when consummation has taken place. It also examines the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on whether any mahr is due. Understanding these nuances is essential for a judge or student of fiqh handling complex cases.

Guided Path
1
Recall the basic case and introduce variations
The basic case gave half mahr each when mahrs are equal, named, and no consummation. Now we examine: (a) mahrs unequal, (b) no named mahr, (c) consummated marriage.
Each variation changes the amount due.
2
Analyze the unequal mahr case
If one mahr is 500 and the other 1000, each woman receives a quarter of her own mahr: 125 and 250 respectively. Total equals half of the sum (750), consistent with one mahr due.
This is derived from the principle of giving half the mahr of the first, then divided equally among the women.
3
Analyze the no-named-mahr case
If no mahr was specified, a single mut'ah (gift) is given to both women collectively, replacing half the mahr. Mut'ah is a lump sum appropriate to the husband's status.
This differs from the named mahr case where the amount is predetermined.
4
Analyze the post-consummation case
If the separation occurs after consummation, each woman receives the full mahr (named or mahr al-mithl). This is because consummation makes full mahr obligatory for the valid wife, and due to ignorance, both receive it.
Here the husband ends up paying two full mahrs, which is a severe outcome.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa: half mahr each (in basic case). Abu Yusuf: nothing due because of total ignorance. Muhammad: full mahr due to each (so two full mahrs). The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's.
The ikhtilaf revolves around the principle of obligation in cases of uncertainty.

Source Text

المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a wife divorces before consummation when no mahr was specified.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable mahr determined by the wife's social status, used when no mahr is named.

8 min
Combining Women Who Are Mahram to Each Other: Mutual vs. One-Sided Prohibition
Ruling on marrying two women with a hypothetical mahram relation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two women who are mahram to each other and distinguish between mutual and one-sided prohibition.

Core Idea
Combining two women is haram only when prohibition is mutual; if only one side, it is allowed.

This passage addresses a subtle point in marriage law: when a man marries two women who are so closely related that if each were male, they would be prohibited from marrying each other. The key is whether the prohibition is reciprocal. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion over which combinations are impermissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining (al-jamʿ) two women in marriage simultaneously. The general ruling is that it is prohibited only if the hypothetical mahram relation holds from both sides.
The example given is a woman and her paternal aunt.
2
Understand the condition of mutual prohibition
For the ruling to be haram, the prohibition must be mutual: if each woman were male, marriage between the two would be impossible due to mahram relations.
If only one side would be prohibited (like a woman and her step-daughter), the combination is permissible.
3
Analyze the opposing view and proof
Zufar and others hold that any one-sided prohibition should make the combination haram out of precaution. Their proof is based on caution.
The Hanafi majority response uses Quran 4:24 and practice of Companions.
4
Identify the Hanafi proof
The majority rely on the general permission of marriage in Quran 4:24 and the fact that there is no blood kinship between the two women, so no severance of ties.
Reports of 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far and Ibn 'Abbas support permissibility in similar cases.
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
Test with other combinations: e.g., a woman and her maternal aunt (mutual? yes, so haram); a woman and her niece (mutual? if niece's father is not the woman's brother, careful). The key is the hypothetical male scenario.
Always verify if both sides are prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبين امرأتين: عطف على قوله بين الأختين أي وحرم الجمع أيضاً بين امرأتين. (ع) حرم النكاح [بينهما كالجمع بين المرأة وعمتها. (ط)] أي بشرط أن ذلك يتصور من الجانبين كالمرأة وعمتها فإن كل واحدة منهما لو فرضت ذكراً حرم العقد بينهما؛ لأنه لو فرضت المرأة ذكراً حرم عليه نكاح . ولو فرضت العمة ذكراً حرم عليه نكاح بنت أخيه، وإذا لم يحرم النكاح بينهما إلا من جهة واحدة جاز الجمع بينهما كما إذا جمع بين امرأة وبنت زوج كان لها من قبل؛ لأن إحداهما لو كان ذكراً الزوجة جاز له أن وهي بالأخرى، فلم يعم التحريم، وقال زفر : لا يجوز؛ لأنه لما ثبت الامتناع من وجه فالأحوط الحرمة وهو مذهب ابن أبي ليلى والحسن البصري وعكرمة، وللجمهور قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُحِلَّ لَكُمْ مَا وَرَاءَ ذَلِكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٢٤) ولأنه لا قرابة بينهما فلم يكن فيه قطيعة الرحم، وقد صح أن عبد بن جعفر جمع بين بنت علي هه وامرأة علي له، وكذا جمع ابن عباس ما بين امرأة رجل وابنته من غيرها، وعند داود وعثمان البتي والخوارج يجوز الجمع بين المحارم غير الأختين.
And between two women: coordinate to his saying 'between two sisters' i.e., also prohibited is combining between two women. ( 'A) Marriage is prohibited [between them, like combining a woman and her paternal aunt. (T)] meaning on condition that this is conceivable from both sides like a woman and her paternal aunt: for if each of them were assumed to be male, marriage between them would be prohibited; because if the woman were male, her marriage to [the aunt] would be prohibited; and if the aunt were male, his marriage to his brother's daughter would be prohibited. But if the prohibition is only from one side, then combining is permissible, as when one combines a woman and the daughter of her husband from a previous marriage; because if one of them [the wife] were male, he could marry the other; so the prohibition does not encompass both. Zufar said: It is not permissible; because since prohibition is established from one side, the precaution is prohibition. This is the madhhab of Ibn Abi Layla, al-Hasan al-Basri, and 'Ikrimah. The majority's proof is the saying of Allah: 'And lawful to you are all beyond this' (4:24), and because there is no kinship between them, so there is no severance of ties of womb. And it is authentically reported that 'Abd [Allah] ibn Ja'far combined between the daughter of 'Ali and the wife of 'Ali, and similarly Ibn 'Abbas combined between a man's wife and his daughter from another [woman]. According to Dawud, 'Uthman al-Batti, and the Khawarij, it is permissible to combine between mahram women other than two sisters.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of combining two women who are so closely related that if each were male, they would be prohibited from marrying each other. The example given is a woman and her paternal aunt (her father's sister). Since if the woman were male, she could not marry her aunt (because she is his aunt), and if the aunt were male, she could not marry her brother's daughter, the prohibition applies from both sides, making it impermissible to marry them simultaneously. However, if the prohibition is only from one side, such as a woman and her step-daughter (the daughter of her husband from another woman), because if the woman were male, she could marry the step-daughter (no blood relation), then combining is permissible. Zufar and some early scholars held it is prohibited out of precaution, but the majority (including the Hanafi school) permit it based on the general permissibility in Quran 4:24 and the practice of the Companions like 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far and Ibn 'Abbas. The text also notes extreme positions where some groups allow combining even close mahram except the two sisters.

Key Terms
الجمع بين المحارم (al-jamʿ bayna al-maharim): Marrying two women who are prohibited to each other due to a hypothetical mahram relation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following combinations is considered haram according to the Hanafi majority?
A) Marrying a woman and her step-daughter.
B) Marrying two sisters.
C) Marrying a woman and her brother's daughter (niece) if the niece is also the wife's daughter?
D) Marrying a woman and her maternal aunt.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of combining two women hinges on the mutuality of the hypothetical mahram relation; if only one side is prohibited, the combination is permissible.

Two Sisters in Two Contracts: Unknown Priority
Ruling on two sisters married in two contracts with unknown priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a man who marries two sisters in two separate contracts without knowing which was first, and calculate the mahr owed in various scenarios.

Core Idea
When the first marriage cannot be identified, the judge annuls both and each sister receives half her specified dower.

This lesson addresses an uncommon but legally instructive scenario: a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts but cannot recall which came first, and he has not consummated either marriage. The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy: both marriages are voided, and each woman receives half her specified dower. The reasoning hinges on legal uncertainty (jahalah) and the principle that the valid first marriage is unknown, so the mahr owed to the first wife is divided between the two. We will also explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and how the same rule applies to other mahram pairs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case and Core Ruling
State the exact scenario: two sisters, two contracts, unknown order, no consummation. The core ruling: the judge separates (annuls) both marriages, and each sister receives half her specified dower.
The ruling assumes both marriages were before consummation.
2
Understand the Legal Reasoning (Ta'lil)
Why half mahr? One marriage is valid (the first), but we cannot identify which. The mahr is due to the first wife, but due to uncertainty it is split equally between the two.
This is not a penalty; it is an equitable division of a known obligation.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that nothing is obligatory due to ignorance (jahalah). Muhammad holds that full mahr is obligatory for each. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is half mahr, as stated in the text.
The mufta bihi balances between the two extremes.
4
Generalize the Principle
The same ruling applies to any pair of women whose simultaneous marriage is prohibited (e.g., a woman and her mother). Also consider variations: different mahr amounts, unspecified mahr, and post-consummation cases.
The text explicitly extends the rule to 'كل من لا يحل جمعه من المحارم'.
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Example: A man marries a woman and her maternal aunt in two contracts, unknown which is first, no consummation. Apply the same ruling: both annulled, each gets half her mahr.
Aunt and niece are also mahram who cannot be married simultaneously.

(ع) نصف المهر: [ أو مسمي واستوى ،مهرهما، وادعت كل أنها الأولى ولا بينة لهما. And if he married two sisters in two contracts, and he does not know which was first, he separates between himself and both of them, and they both get half the dower. And between two women, whichever of them is assumed to be male, marriage is prohibited, i.e., whichever of his women is from them. 11 i.e., the judge separates the man from the two sisters, i.e., the two mentioned sisters, in two contracts. And likewise every woman whose collection with her is not permissible among the mahrams, like a woman and her mother. (T) Mentioning sisters is not a restriction; rather, he married two women from those whose collection is not permissible in marriage among the mahrams as such. And he restricted it to two contracts because if they were in one contract, both would be invalid, so no dower is obligatory for them except by intercourse. And his saying: 'and he does not know which was first' is a precaution for the case when he knows which was first, for then the first contract is valid, so her intercourse is permissible unless he had intercourse with the second, then the first becomes prohibited as long as the second is in her waiting period, and intercourse with the second is not permissible due to the invalidity of the contract. (Ayni, Fath) 'And he does not know which was first': i.e., the first contract, and he did not have intercourse with either of them. (T, A) 'We do not know between him and them': i.e., between the man and the two sisters; because the marriage of one of them is definitely invalid, and there is no basis for specification due to lack of priority. (A) 'Half the dower': [or the specified dower and equal, their dower, and each claims she is the first and there is no evidence for them. (T)] because it was obligatory for the first of them, so it is given to them due to lack of priority. This is if each of them claims that she is the first and there is no evidence for them. But if they say: 'Which of the two marriages was first?', nothing is decreed for them because the one decreed for is unknown and ignorance prevents the validity of the decree unless they agree to take half the dower, then it is decreed for them. From Abu Yusuf: nothing is obligatory for them due to ignorance. From Muhammad: the full dower is obligatory. Then this is if their dowers are equal and it is specified in the contract, and the divorce was before consummation. If they are different, one-fourth of her dower is decreed for each. If it was not specified in the contract, one single gift (mut'ah) is obligatory for them in place of half the dower. If the separation is after consummation, the full dower is obligatory for each. And all that has been mentioned of rulings between two sisters is the ruling between every pair whose collection is not permissible among the mahrams. Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/195]
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with intra-Hanafi dispute. It deals with the case where a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts but does not know which contract was first, and he has not consummated either marriage. The qadi must annul both marriages and order half the specified dower for each sister. The reasoning is that the first marriage is valid, but since we cannot identify it, we treat both as equally likely; the dower is prescribed for the first wife, but due to uncertainty it is divided equally. Abu Yusuf holds nothing is due because of ignorance, while Muhammad holds full dower is due. The same rule applies to any pair of women who cannot be simultaneously married (e.g., a woman and her mother). If the mahr is not specified, a single mut'ah (compensatory gift) is given instead of half the mahr. If consummation occurred, each gets full mahr.

Key Terms
فرق بينه وبينهما (farraqa baynahu wa baynahuma): The judge separates (annuls) the marriage between the man and both women.
نصف المهر (nisf al-mahr): Half the specified dower; paid when divorce occurs before consummation.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the identity of the first wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries two sisters in two contracts without knowing which was first, and divorces before consummation, what is the ruling according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Both marriages are valid; he keeps both.
B) Both marriages are annulled; each sister gets half the dower.
C) Only the first marriage is valid; the second is void.
D) No dower is given because of uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
When uncertain which of two prohibited marriages occurred first, the Hanafi school annuls both and awards half the dower to each woman.

Mutual Mahramiyyah: The Rule of Two-Sided Prohibition
Ruling on collecting two women with mutual mahramiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on collecting two women who are mahram from both sides and apply the condition of mutual prohibition.

Core Idea
Marrying two women is prohibited only when each would be mahram to the other if male.

In the laws of marriage, certain women are permanently prohibited due to blood, affinity, or fosterage. But what about marrying two women who are not related to each other by blood, yet each is mahram to the other through marriage? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the prohibition applies only when the relationship is mutual. We'll explore the ruling, the evidence, and the scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under discussion is collecting (الجمع) two women in marriage simultaneously. The ruling depends on whether the two women are mahram to each other if each were male.
We are not considering the man's own mahram relationship to each woman, but the relationship between the two women.
2
State the condition for prohibition
Prohibition arises only when the relationship is mutual: if each woman, when assumed to be male, would be prohibited to marry the other. For example, a woman and her paternal aunt: if the woman were a man, she cannot marry her aunt; if the aunt were a man, she cannot marry her niece.
This is called 'two-sided mahramiyyah'.
3
Apply the one-sided exception
If the prohibition is only one-sided, collection is permissible. Example: a woman and the daughter of her husband from a previous marriage. If the woman were a man, she could marry the daughter; if the daughter were a man, she could marry the woman? Actually the text gives a different example: a woman and the daughter of her husband from before. In that case, if the woman were male, she could marry the daughter (since the daughter is not his mahram), but if the daughter were male, she could not marry the woman because the woman would be his stepmother? Let's verify: The text says 'as when he collects between a woman and the daughter of a husband she had from before; because if one of them were male, the wife would be permissible for him to marry the other.' So the prohibition is only one-sided.
The example shows that if only one direction is prohibited, collection is allowed.
4
Understand the dispute
Zufar and some early scholars (Ibn Abi Layla, Hasan al-Basri, Ikrimah) held that even if the prohibition is from one side, precaution requires forbidding collection. The Hanafi school and the majority disagree.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Analyze the evidence
The Hanafi proof includes: Quran 4:24 (general permissibility of marrying women beyond those mentioned), absence of kinship ties (no cutting of womb), and the practice of companions (Abd ibn Ja'far and Ibn Abbas). Zufar's position is based on precaution (ihtiyat).
The majority view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبين امرأتين: عطف على قوله بين الأختين أي وحرم الجمع أيضاً بين امرأتين. (ع) حرم النكاح [بينهما كالجمع بين المرأة وعمتها. (ط)] أي بشرط أن ذلك يتصور من الجانبين كالمرأة وعمتها، فإن كل واحدة منهما لو فرضت ذكراً حرم العقد بينهما؛ لأنه لو فرضت المرأة ذكراً حرم عليه نكاح . ولو فرضت العمة ذكراً حرم عليه نكاح بنت أخيه، وإذا لم يحرم النكاح بينهما إلا من جهة واحدة جاز الجمع بينهما كما إذا جمع بين امرأة وبنت زوج كان لها من قبل؛ لأن إحداهما لو كان ذكراً الزوجة جاز له أن وهي بالأخرى، فلم يعم التحريم، وقال زفر : لا يجوز؛ لأنه لما ثبت الامتناع من وجه فالأحوط الحرمة وهو مذهب ابن أبي ليلى والحسن البصري وعكرمة، وللجمهور قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُحِلَّ لَكُمْ مَا وَرَاءَ ذَلِكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٢٤) ولأنه لا قرابة بينهما فلم يكن فيه قطيعة الرحم، وقد صح أن عبد بن جعفر جمع بين بنت علي هه وامرأة علي له، وكذا جمع ابن عباس ما بين امرأة رجل وابنته من غيرها، وعند داود وعثمان البتي والخوارج يجوز الجمع بين المحارم غير الأختين. (فتح عيني)
And between two women: it is a conjunction to his saying 'between two sisters', i.e., collection is also prohibited between two women. (A) Marriage is prohibited between them like the collection between a woman and her paternal aunt. (T) i.e., on the condition that it is conceivable from both sides, like a woman and her paternal aunt. For each of them, if assumed to be male, the contract between them would be prohibited; because if the woman were assumed male, marrying her would be prohibited, and if the paternal aunt were assumed male, marrying the daughter of his brother would be prohibited. And if the prohibition of marriage between them is only from one side, collection is permissible, as when he collects between a woman and the daughter of a husband she had from before; because if one of them were male, the wife would be permissible for him to marry the other, so the prohibition is not general. Zufar said: It is not permissible; because when prohibition is established from one aspect, the precaution is prohibition; and this is the school of Ibn Abi Layla, al-Hasan al-Basri, and Ikrimah. And for the majority is the saying of Allah: {And lawful to you are those beyond that} (4:24), and because there is no kinship between them, so there is no cutting of ties of womb. And it is authentically reported that Abd ibn Ja'far collected between the daughter of Ali, [may Allah be pleased with him], and the wife of Ali, [may Allah be pleased with him]; and similarly Ibn Abbas collected between the wife of a man and his daughter from another woman. And according to Dawud, Uthman al-Batti, and the Khawarij, collection is permissible among mahrams other than sisters. (Fath al-Qadir, Ayni)
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It explains the rule about marrying two women who are not blood-related but become mahram due to affinity (musahara) from both sides. If each woman, when assumed to be male, would be a mahram to the other, collection is prohibited. For example, a woman and her paternal aunt: if the woman were a man, she could not marry her aunt because she is her aunt; if the aunt were a man, she could not marry her niece. So collection is prohibited. But if the prohibition is only one-sided, collection is allowed, e.g., a woman and the daughter of her husband from a previous marriage: if the woman were a man, she could marry the daughter; if the daughter were a man, she could marry the mother? Actually the text gives a different example. The Hanafi position is with the majority, citing Quran 4:24 and the practice of companions. Zufar and others hold precautionary prohibition. The passage ends with noting that Dawud, al-Batti, and Khawarij allow collection among mahrams except sisters.

Key Terms
المحارم (al-maharim): Those women who are permanently prohibited to marry due to blood, affinity, or fosterage.
الجمع بين المحارم (al-jam' bayn al-maharim): Collecting two women who are mahram to each other in marriage simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Prohibited because both sides make each other mahram.

Key Takeaway
Collection of two women is prohibited only when each woman would be forbidden to the other if both were male.

Unlawful Acts and Affinity Prohibitions in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling that zina and lustful touch/look create affinity prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zina, lustful touch, and lustful look establish affinity prohibitions, identify the four prohibitions, and explain the Hanafi proof from Quran 4:22 and hadith.

Core Idea
Unlawful intercourse and lustful touch/look create the same affinity prohibitions as lawful marriage—because the cause is shared.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi ruling: that zina (unlawful intercourse) and even lustful touch or look create permanent marriage prohibitions (hurmah al-musaharah). This extends the prohibitions of affinity beyond lawful marriage. The passage defines the acts, the condition of desire, and the scope of prohibitions. It also presents a refutation of the Shafi'i position, which restricts these prohibitions to lawful marital relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that zina, touching, and looking with desire establish 'hurmah al-musaharah' (affinity prohibitions). The ruling applies to both men and women, intentionally or mistakenly, coerced or forgetful.
Note that the act itself is sinful (haram), but the prohibition it creates is a separate legal effect.
2
Understand the conditions for the prohibition
Desire (al-shahwah) is defined: for men, erection or increased erection; for women, heart disturbance. Ejaculation during touch or look negates the prohibition. The woman must be 'desirable' (mushatah), and a nine-year-old girl is considered desirable. Anal intercourse does not create the prohibition.
The condition of no ejaculation for touch/look is critical—if he ejaculates, no prohibition is established.
3
List the four prohibitions that arise
If a man commits zina with a woman, or touches/looks with desire: (1) She becomes haram to his father (and his grandfathers, etc.), (2) to his sons (and grandsons, etc.). Similarly, (3) the man becomes haram to her mother (and grandmothers, etc.), and (4) to her daughter (and granddaughters, etc.).
These are the same prohibitions that arise from lawful marriage.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The primary proof is Quran 4:22—'And do not marry what your fathers married'—where 'nikah' is interpreted as intercourse (wat'), thus including zina. Hadiths about looking and touching with desire are cited. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection (that the unlawful cannot make the lawful unlawful) is that the cause (illa) is the potential for lineage, shared by both lawful and unlawful intercourse.
The Hanafi principle here is that the legal cause ('illa) is the act of penetration (or its prelude in touch/look), not the lawfulness of the act.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i view and see the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that unlawful acts cannot create lawful prohibitions, citing a hadith. The Hanafi response uses the reasoning of shared causality and cites support from many Companions (Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, Aisha, etc.).
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi may not marry the mother/daughter of a woman with whom he committed zina, while a Shafi'i may.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والزنا واللمس والنظر بشهوة يوجب حرمة المصاهرة، وحرم تزوّج والزنا: مبتدأ خبره "يوجب" وهو الوطء في قبل خال عن ملك الزاني وشبهته (ع) واللمس: عطف على "الزنا" سواء كان من الرجل أو المرأة عمداً أو خطأ أو مكرها أو ناسيا. (ع) والنظر إلى الفرج الداخل من جانبه أو من جانبها. (ط،ع) يوجب حرمة المصاهرة : أي من زنى بامرأة أو مسها بشهوة أو نظر إلى فرجها الداخل بشهوة، أو المرأة مسته بشهوة، أو نظرت إلى ذكره بشهوة يثبت بها حرمات أربع تحرم هي على آباء الواطئ وإن علوا، وعلى أولاده وإن سفلوا، وتحرم على الواطئ أمهاتها وإن علون وبناتها وإن سفلن وحد الشهوة في الرجل أن ينتشر آلته أو يزداد انتشاره لو كان منتشراً، وفي المرأة تحرك القلب على وجه يشوش الخاطر، ووجودها . أحدهما من يكفي، والشرط أن لا ينزل حتى لو أنزل عند المس أو النظر لم يثبت به حرمة المصاهرة، وكذا لو وطئ في دبر المرأة لا يثبت به، وفي الشيخ الكبير والمحبوب والعنين يعتبر تحرك القلب، ويشترط أن تكون المرأة مشتهاة ، وبنت تسع مشتهاة، وقال الشافعي: الزنا والمس والنظر لا يوجب حرمة المصاهرة؛ لقوله علية: "لا يحرم الحرام الحلال"؛ ولأنها نعمة لا تنال بالمحظور، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَنْكِحُوا مَا نَكَحَ آبَاؤُكُمْ (النساء: ٢٢) والنكاح هو الوطء. ولهذا حرم على الابن ما وطئ أبوه بملك اليمين فعم الزنا؛ ولأن وطء الحلال لم يكن سبباً للحرمة؛ لكونه حلالاً، بل لكونه سبباً للجزئية بواسطة الولد والحرام شارك الحلال في السببية، فيشاركه في الحرمة، وقال الشافعي في المس والنظر: إنما إن كانا في محل مباح بأن كانا من زوجته فإنهما ليسا في معنى الدخول، ولهذا لا يتعلق بهما فساد الصوم والإحرام، ووجوب الغسل، ولا يلحقان بالدخول، ولنا: قوله عليه: "من نظر إلى فرج امرأة لم تحل له أمها ولا بنتها"، وقوله عليها: "لو امرأة بشهوة حرمت عليه أمها وبنتها"، ولأنهما سببان داعيان إلى الوطء فيقامان مقامه في موضع الاحتياط، وهو مذهب عمر وعمران بن الحصين وجابر بن عبد الله وأبي بن كعب وعائشة وابن مسعود وابن عباس له وجمهور التابعين له . (عيني، مسكين، مستخلص)
And zina, touching, and looking with desire establish the prohibition of affinity. Zina: a subject whose predicate is 'establishes', and it is intercourse in the front free from ownership of the fornicator and its doubt. (A) Touching: conjunct to 'zina', whether from the man or woman, intentionally or mistakenly, coerced or forgetful. (A) And looking at the internal private part from his side or her side. (T, A) Establishes prohibition of affinity: i.e., whoever commits zina with a woman, or touches her with desire, or looks at her internal private part with desire, or the woman touches him with desire, or looks at his penis with desire, then four prohibitions are established: she becomes prohibited to the fornicator's fathers even if high, and to his children even if low, and she becomes prohibited to the fornicator's mothers even if high and daughters even if low. And the definition of desire in the man is that his organ becomes erect or increases in erection if it was already erect, and in the woman is the movement of the heart in a way that disturbs the mind. The existence of one of them is sufficient. The condition is that he does not ejaculate; if he ejaculates upon touching or looking, the affinity prohibition is not established by it, and likewise if he penetrates in the anus of the woman it is not established. For the elderly, the beloved, and the impotent, the movement of the heart is considered. And it is required that the woman be desirable, and a nine-year-old girl is desirable. Al-Shafi'i said: Zina, touching, and looking do not establish affinity prohibition because of his saying: 'The unlawful does not make the lawful unlawful', and because it is a blessing not attained by prohibition. Our proof is the saying of Allah: {And do not marry what your fathers married} (4:22), and marriage is intercourse. For this reason, what a father owned by right hand is prohibited to the son, so zina is encompassed. And because lawful intercourse is not a cause for prohibition due to being lawful, but rather because it is a cause for partiality through the child, and the unlawful shares the causal nature with the lawful, so it shares in the prohibition. Al-Shafi'i said regarding touching and looking: only if they occur in a permissible place, such as from his wife, then they are not in the meaning of entry, and therefore the invalidation of fasting and ihram and the obligation of ghusl are not attached to them, and they are not equated to entry. Our proof is his saying: 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and daughter are not permissible for him', and his saying: 'If he touches a woman with desire, her mother and daughter become prohibited to him'. And because they are two causes that invite to intercourse, so they stand in its place in precautionary matters. This is the school of Umar, Imran ibn Husayn, Jabir ibn Abdullah, Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Aisha, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, and the majority of the Followers. (Ayni, Miskin, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It establishes that zina (unlawful intercourse), touching, and looking with desire create perpetual affinity prohibitions similar to lawful marriage. The text defines zina as vaginal intercourse without ownership or its doubt. Touching and looking include both genders and various states. The prohibitions are fourfold: the woman becomes mahram to the man's ascendants and descendants, and the man becomes mahram to her ascendants and descendants. The definition of desire differs: for men, erection; for women, heart disturbance. Ejaculation or anal intercourse nullifies the effect. The Shafi'i school opposes, arguing that unlawful acts cannot lawful things, but Hanafis cite Quran 4:22 and hadiths, applying analogy that both lawful and unlawful intercourse share the same causal effect of creating affinity. The text also notes that looking at the private part or touching with desire also establish the prohibition based on hadiths and the principle of precaution.

Key Terms
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmah al-musaharah): The perpetual marriage prohibition established through affinity (by marriage or by zina/touch/look).
الشهوة (al-shahwah): Desire; defined by erection in men and heart disturbance in women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does looking at a woman's private part with desire establish the prohibition of marrying her mother?
A) Yes, based on the hadith 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and daughter are not permissible for him'.
B) No, because looking does not create affinity.
C) Yes, only if ejaculation occurs.
D) No, only zina establishes such prohibitions.

Key Takeaway
Zina, lustful touch, and lustful look establish the same affinity prohibitions as lawful marriage in Hanafi fiqh, based on the shared cause of potential lineage.
