The Three Types of Firash and Their Effect on Lineage
Definition of three bed types for lineage establishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of firash and explain how lineage is established or negated for each type.

Core Idea
Child lineage follows the firash: strong requires li'an to deny, medium allows simple denial, weak needs a claim.

This passage introduces a foundational classification in Hanafi family law. The type of marital relationship a man has with a woman directly determines the rules for attributing a child to him. Understanding these three categories is essential for any student of fiqh dealing with lineage and paternity issues.

Guided Path
1
Define firash
Understand that firash is the legal status of a woman such that a child born to her is attributed to the man without need for his acknowledgment.
The term 'bed' metaphorically refers to the marital relationship.
2
Identify the three types
Recognize that firash is divided into strong (qawi), medium (wasat), and weak (da'if).
Memorize this trichotomy.
3
Learn the rule for establishment of lineage
For strong and medium firash, lineage is established automatically; for weak, it requires a claim (da'wa).
4
Learn the rule for negation of lineage
Strong firash can only be negated by li'an (mutual oath); medium by simple denial; weak requires no negation since lineage is not established without claim.
Li'an is a specific legal procedure.
5
Apply the classification to examples
Practice with scenarios: a married free woman (strong), a concubine who has borne a child (medium), a slave woman without child (weak).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الفراش ثلاثة أنواع: قوي ووسط وضعيف، فالقوي فراش المنكوحة يثبت نسب ولدها بلا إقرار، ولا ينتفي إلا باللعان، والوسط: فراش أم الولد يثبت النسب بلا إقرار، وينتفي بمجرد النفي والضعيف: فراش الأمة لا يثبت نسب ولدها بلا دعوة، ومعنى الفراش صيرورة المرأة بحال لو جاءت بولد ثبت نسبه من غير دعوة (مستخلص، فتح عيني)
Then know that the bed (firash) is of three types: strong, medium, and weak. The strong is the bed of the married wife; the lineage of her child is established without acknowledgment and is not negated except by li'an. The medium: the bed of the umm al-walad; lineage is established without acknowledgment and is negated merely by denial. The weak: the bed of the slave woman; the lineage of her child is not established without a claim. The meaning of bed is that the woman becomes in a state such that if she brings a child, its lineage is established without a claim. (Mukhtasar, Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This is a definition passage explaining the three types of marital bed (firash) in Hanafi law, which determine how lineage is established. The strong bed is that of a free wife in a valid marriage: her child is automatically attributed to the husband, and he can only deny it through li'an (oath of condemnation). The medium bed is that of a concubine who has borne a child (umm al-walad): her child's lineage is also established automatically but can be denied simply by the master's denial without li'an. The weak bed is that of a slave woman: her child is not attributed to the owner unless he explicitly claims it. The term 'firash' refers to the status of the woman such that if she bears a child, the child is linked to the man without him needing to make a claim. This classification is foundational for rules of paternity and inheritance.

Key Terms
الفراش (al-firash): The legal status of a woman such that a child born to her is attributed to the man without claim
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual oath of condemnation between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of firash requires a claim for lineage to be established?
A) Strong
B) Medium
C) Weak
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The type of firash determines whether a child's lineage is automatically established or requires a claim, and how paternity can be denied.

Nikah — Marriage

Invalidity of Mut'ah Marriage and Its Abrogation
Proof and explanation of mut'ah marriage being invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah marriage, cite the dalil for its invalidity, and explain the refutation of the opposing view.

Core Idea
Mut'ah marriage is invalid and haram; those who legalize it become disbelievers.

Mut'ah marriage was temporarily permitted in early Islam but was later abrogated by clear textual evidence and the consensus of the Companions. This lesson establishes the Hanafi position that temporary marriage is batil, examines the proof from hadith and Quran, and refutes the allowance claimed by some based on Quran 4:24. The ruling is severe: anyone who considers it permissible exits the fold of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on mut'ah marriage
Note that the text begins by stating mut'ah marriage is invalid (batil) and explains its historical permission and subsequent abrogation.
The ruling is definitive, with a strong consequence for those who legalize it.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Locate the dalil: the hadith of Ali (ra) that the Prophet (saw) forbade mut'ah on the day of Khaybar (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim) and another narration forbidding it on the day of the Conquest of Makkah. Also note the Quranic proof from Surah al-Mu'minun (23:6) limiting sexual relations to wives and slave women.
The prohibition (nahy) is explicit and abrogates earlier permission.
3
Analyze the opposing school's argument
Identify the opposing view attributed to Ibn Abbas and the Shi'a, who cite Quran 4:24 as evidence for the permissibility of mut'ah.
They interpret 'enjoy' (istimta') as temporary marriage.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that Quran 4:24 refers to permanent marriage with mahr, not temporary marriage. The hadith of prohibition abrogates any apparent permission. Additionally, the verse from Surah al-Mu'minun excludes mut'ah because it is not proper marriage (no maintenance, inheritance, etc.) and not slavery.
The abrogation is established by both naskh (supersession) and ijma' al-sahabah.
5
Note the practical consequence
Any marriage contract with a fixed term is void in the Hanafi school. Those who consider it valid are deemed outside the fold, though no corporal punishment applies for contracting it.
The thamarah al-khilaf is fundamental: Hanafis reject temporary marriage outright.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل نكاح المتعة وهذا كان مباحاً أيام خيبر، وأيام فتح مكة إلا أنها صارت منسوخة بإجماع الصحابة، ولو أباحه أحد صار كافراً لكن ليس فيه تعزير ولا حد ولا رجم، واشتهر عن ابن عباس لما تحليلها، وتبعه على ذلك أكثر أصحابه من أهل اليمن ومكة، وكان يستدل على ذلك بقوله: ﴿فَمَا اسْتَمْتَعْتُمْ بِهِ مِنْهُنَّ فَآتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ﴾ (النساء: ٢٤) وإليه ذهبت الشيعة، وخالفوا عليا الله وأكثر أصحابه، والحجة عليهم ما روي أنه عليها حرمها يوم خيبر" من رواية علي بن أبي طالب الله متفق عليه، وروي أنه علي حرمها يوم الفتح، رواه مسلم، وقال بعضهم: نسخت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ هُمْ لِفُرُوجِهِمْ حَافِظُونَ إِلَّا عَلَى أَزْوَاجِهِمْ أَوْ مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُهُمْ ﴾ (المؤمنون:٦) وهي ليست من الأزواج بدليل انتفاء حكم النكاح عنها، وانتفاء شرطه من وجوب النفقة والسكنى والطلاق والعدة والإرث والشهود، ولا هي ملكته الأيمان فثبت نسخه، وروي عن ابن عباس أنه أمسك عن الفتوى بها، وقال له علي ه: إنك تائه أن النبي النهي عن متعة النساء"، رواه مسلم، والمراد في الآية الاستمتاع منهن بالنكاح والمهر يسمى أجرة، قال الله تعالى: فَانْكِحُوهُنَّ بِإِذْنِ أَهْلِهِنَّ وَآتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ﴾ (النساء:٢٥) [رمز الحقائق: ١٩٨/١] واعلم أن المتعة على أربعة أوجه اثنتان في الحج واثنتان في النكاح، أما في الحج فإحداهما مشروعة ذكر في باب التمتع في الحج، والأخرى منسوخة وهي فسخ إحرام الحج بأفعال العمرة، وهذا قد كان ثم نسخ، وأما في النكاح فإحداهما مشروعة؛ لقوله تعالى: إِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ مَا لَمْ تَمَسُّوهُنَّ أَوْ تَفْرِضُوا لَهُنَّ فَرِيضَةً وَمَتِّعُوهُنَّ (البقرة:٢٣٦)، وهي ثلاثة أثواب درع وحمار وملحفة، والأخرى غير مشروعة وهي نكاح المتعة بأن يقول لامرأة أتمتع بك كذا مدة بكذا من المال، أو يقول متعيني نفسك بكذا من الدراهم مدة كذا فتقول: متعتك نفسي، ولابد . لفظ التمتع في هذا النكاح، ويشترط فيها تعيين مقدار المهر. (فتح) من
And mut'ah marriage is invalid. It was permissible during the days of Khaybar and the days of the conquest of Makkah, but it became abrogated by consensus of the Companions. If anyone legalizes it, he becomes a disbeliever, but there is no ta'zir, hadd, or rajm (for doing it). It is well-known that Ibn Abbas held it permissible, and most of his followers from Yemen and Makkah followed him. He used to argue with His saying: 'So whatever you enjoy from them, give them their due compensation' (4:24). The Shi'a adopted this view and opposed Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and most of his Companions. The proof against them is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade it on the day of Khaybar from the narration of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) agreed upon, and it is narrated that he forbade it on the day of Conquest, narrated by Muslim. Some said it was abrogated by His saying: 'And those who guard their private parts except from their wives or those their right hands possess' (23:6). It (mut'ah wife) is not among wives because the rulings of marriage are absent: lack of obligation of maintenance, housing, divorce, waiting period, inheritance, and witnesses; nor is she among those their right hands possess, so its abrogation is established. It is narrated that Ibn Abbas refrained from giving fatwa on it, and Ali said to him: 'You are lost, the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade mut'ah of women' narrated by Muslim. The meaning in the verse is enjoyment of them through marriage and the mahr is called a wage. Allah said: 'So marry them with the permission of their families and give them their due compensation' (4:25). [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/198] And know that mut'ah is of four types: two in hajj and two in marriage. As for hajj, one is prescribed mentioned in the chapter on tamattu' in hajj, the other is abrogated, which is annulling the ihram of hajj with the actions of umrah; this existed then was abrogated. As for marriage, one is prescribed due to His saying: 'If you divorce women before touching them or specifying an obligation, then give them a gift' (2:236), and it is three garments: a shift, a [....], and a cloak. The other is not prescribed, which is mut'ah marriage: that he says to a woman 'I enjoy you for such a period for such money,' or she says 'I give myself to you for such dirhams for such period' and she says 'I have given myself,' and the word 'enjoyment' in this marriage is necessary, and specification of the amount of mahr is required. (Fath)
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive ruling on mut'ah (temporary) marriage. It states that mut'ah marriage is invalid (batil) in the Hanafi school. It was initially permitted in early Islam (during Khaybar and Conquest of Makkah) but was abrogated by the consensus of the Companions and clear ahadith. The severe position is that anyone who considers it permissible becomes a disbeliever, though no corporal punishment applies to those who contract it. The passage refutes the position of Ibn Abbas (who allowed it early on) and the Shi'a, using the hadith from Ali (ra) that the Prophet (saw) forbade it. Evidence of abrogation also comes from the verse in Surah al-Mu'minun, which confines sexual relations to wives and slave women; a mut'ah wife is neither. The passage ends by distinguishing different types of mut'ah: two related to hajj (one valid, one abrogated) and two in marriage (one valid—the post-divorce gift—and one invalid—temporary marriage). The invalid form requires the word 'tamattu'' and specification of mahr and duration.

Key Terms
نكاح المتعة (nikah al-mut'ah): A marriage contracted for a specified time period in exchange for compensation
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Enjoyment; can refer to temporary marriage or to a gift given to a divorced woman

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah marriage?
A) Permissible with conditions
B) Invalid and its legalizer becomes a disbeliever
C) Valid but disliked
D) Valid only if witnessed

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah marriage is invalid and haram; any contract with a fixed term is void, and those who believe it permissible leave the fold of Islam.

The Four Types of Mut'ah in Hajj and Marriage
Classification of four types of mut'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four types of mut'ah, distinguish which are prescribed and which are abrogated, and explain the legal status of each.

Core Idea
Mut'ah has four types: two in hajj (one valid tamattu', one abrogated) and two in marriage (one prescribed gift, one invalid temporary marriage).

The term 'mut'ah' appears in different contexts in Islamic law, leading to confusion. This passage clarifies that there are four distinct types of mut'ah: two related to hajj and two related to marriage. One in each category is prescribed and one is abrogated or impermissible. Understanding this classification prevents conflating the recommended tamattu' in hajj with the prohibited temporary marriage.

Guided Path
1
Understand the fourfold classification
Note that the text divides mut'ah into four types: two in hajj and two in nikah. This is the key framework.
This is a mnemonic and conceptual clarification.
2
Identify the two types in hajj
One is prescribed: tamattu' in hajj (performing umrah and hajj with ihram in the same trip). One is abrogated: annulling the ihram of hajj to perform umrah mid-hajj.
3
Identify the two types in marriage
One is prescribed: the post-divorce gift (mut'at al-talaq) mentioned in Quran 2:236. One is abrogated/impermissible: temporary marriage (nikah al-mut'ah).
4
Examine the prescribed mut'ah in marriage
The prescribed mut'ah (tamattu') is a gift given to a divorced woman, especially if no mahr was specified and/or before consummation. The text specifies it consists of three garments.
This is an obligatory gift (wajib) according to some, recommended according to others.
5
Distinguish the impermissible type
The impermissible type is the temporary marriage contract (nikah al-mut'ah) which requires the word 'tamattu'' and specification of duration and mahr. This is exactly the mut'ah discussed in the previous lesson.
It is invalid (batil) and haram.

وبطل نكاح المتعة وهذا كان مباحاً أيام خيبر، وأيام فتح مكة إلا أنها صارت منسوخة بإجماع الصحابة، ولو أباحه أحد صار كافراً لكن ليس فيه تعزير ولا حد ولا رجم، واشتهر عن ابن عباس لما تحليلها، وتبعه على ذلك أكثر أصحابه من أهل اليمن ومكة، وكان يستدل على ذلك بقوله: ﴿فَمَا اسْتَمْتَعْتُمْ بِهِ مِنْهُنَّ فَآتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ﴾ (النساء: ٢٤) وإليه ذهبت الشيعة، وخالفوا عليا الله وأكثر أصحابه، والحجة عليهم ما روي أنه عليها حرمها يوم خيبر" من رواية علي بن أبي طالب الله متفق عليه، وروي أنه علي حرمها يوم الفتح، رواه مسلم، وقال بعضهم: نسخت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ هُمْ لِفُرُوجِهِمْ حَافِظُونَ إِلَّا عَلَى أَزْوَاجِهِمْ أَوْ مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُهُمْ ﴾ (المؤمنون:٦) وهي ليست من الأزواج بدليل انتفاء حكم النكاح عنها، وانتفاء شرطه من وجوب النفقة والسكنى والطلاق والعدة والإرث والشهود، ولا هي ملكته الأيمان فثبت نسخه، وروي عن ابن عباس أنه أمسك عن الفتوى بها، وقال له علي ه: إنك تائه أن النبي النهي عن متعة النساء"، رواه مسلم، والمراد في الآية الاستمتاع منهن بالنكاح والمهر يسمى أجرة، قال الله تعالى: فَانْكِحُوهُنَّ بِإِذْنِ أَهْلِهِنَّ وَآتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ﴾ (النساء:٢٥) [رمز الحقائق: ١٩٨/١] واعلم أن المتعة على أربعة أوجه اثنتان في الحج واثنتان في النكاح، أما في الحج فإحداهما مشروعة ذكر في باب التمتع في الحج، والأخرى منسوخة وهي فسخ إحرام الحج بأفعال العمرة، وهذا قد كان ثم نسخ، وأما في النكاح فإحداهما مشروعة؛ لقوله تعالى: إِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ مَا لَمْ تَمَسُّوهُنَّ أَوْ تَفْرِضُوا لَهُنَّ فَرِيضَةً وَمَتِّعُوهُنَّ (البقرة:٢٣٦)، وهي ثلاثة أثواب درع وحمار وملحفة، والأخرى غير مشروعة وهي نكاح المتعة بأن يقول لامرأة أتمتع بك كذا مدة بكذا من المال، أو يقول متعيني نفسك بكذا من الدراهم مدة كذا فتقول: متعتك نفسي، ولابد . لفظ التمتع في هذا النكاح، ويشترط فيها تعيين مقدار المهر. (فتح) من
And mut'ah marriage is invalid. It was permissible during the days of Khaybar and the days of the conquest of Makkah, but it became abrogated by consensus of the Companions. If anyone legalizes it, he becomes a disbeliever, but there is no ta'zir, hadd, or rajm (for doing it). It is well-known that Ibn Abbas held it permissible, and most of his followers from Yemen and Makkah followed him. He used to argue with His saying: 'So whatever you enjoy from them, give them their due compensation' (4:24). The Shi'a adopted this view and opposed Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and most of his Companions. The proof against them is what is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade it on the day of Khaybar from the narration of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) agreed upon, and it is narrated that he forbade it on the day of Conquest, narrated by Muslim. Some said it was abrogated by His saying: 'And those who guard their private parts except from their wives or those their right hands possess' (23:6). It (mut'ah wife) is not among wives because the rulings of marriage are absent: lack of obligation of maintenance, housing, divorce, waiting period, inheritance, and witnesses; nor is she among those their right hands possess, so its abrogation is established. It is narrated that Ibn Abbas refrained from giving fatwa on it, and Ali said to him: 'You are lost, the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade mut'ah of women' narrated by Muslim. The meaning in the verse is enjoyment of them through marriage and the mahr is called a wage. Allah said: 'So marry them with the permission of their families and give them their due compensation' (4:25). [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/198] And know that mut'ah is of four types: two in hajj and two in marriage. As for hajj, one is prescribed mentioned in the chapter on tamattu' in hajj, the other is abrogated, which is annulling the ihram of hajj with the actions of umrah; this existed then was abrogated. As for marriage, one is prescribed due to His saying: 'If you divorce women before touching them or specifying an obligation, then give them a gift' (2:236), and it is three garments: a shift, a [....], and a cloak. The other is not prescribed, which is mut'ah marriage: that he says to a woman 'I enjoy you for such a period for such money,' or she says 'I give myself to you for such dirhams for such period' and she says 'I have given myself,' and the word 'enjoyment' in this marriage is necessary, and specification of the amount of mahr is required. (Fath)
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive ruling on mut'ah (temporary) marriage. It states that mut'ah marriage is invalid (batil) in the Hanafi school. It was initially permitted in early Islam (during Khaybar and Conquest of Makkah) but was abrogated by the consensus of the Companions and clear ahadith. The severe position is that anyone who considers it permissible becomes a disbeliever, though no corporal punishment applies to those who contract it. The passage refutes the position of Ibn Abbas (who allowed it early on) and the Shi'a, using the hadith from Ali (ra) that the Prophet (saw) forbade it. Evidence of abrogation also comes from the verse in Surah al-Mu'minun, which confines sexual relations to wives and slave women; a mut'ah wife is neither. The passage ends by distinguishing different types of mut'ah: two related to hajj (one valid, one abrogated) and two in marriage (one valid—the post-divorce gift—and one invalid—temporary marriage). The invalid form requires the word 'tamattu'' and specification of mahr and duration.

Key Terms
نكاح المتعة (nikah al-mut'ah): A marriage contracted for a specified time period in exchange for compensation; one of the four types of mut'ah, and it is impermissible.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Enjoyment; in hajj it refers to performing umrah and hajj in one journey; in marriage it can refer to the post-divorce gift or to temporary marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many types of mut'ah are there according to the passage?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
There are four distinct types of mut'ah; only the post-divorce gift and the hajj tamattu' are prescribed, while temporary marriage and the abrogated hajj practice are not.

Nikah — Marriage

Invalidity of Muwaqqat Marriage
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muwaqqat marriage, explain the proof that perpetuity is a condition, and differentiate it from mut'ah.

Core Idea
Marriage must be perpetual; a time-limited marriage is void because its purpose requires permanence.

This passage tackles the controversial issue of time-limited marriage. While Imam Zufar of the Hanafi school considered it valid with a void condition, the majority Hanafi position declares it completely invalid. The author also distinguishes it from mut'ah and addresses an exceptional case where the time limit is so long it effectively means lifelong cohabitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the disputed issue
The passage opens by stating that muwaqqat marriage is invalid. Identify that the dispute is about whether the marriage is completely void or valid with a void condition.
The ruling is batil (completely invalid) according to the majority.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi proof (لنا) is given: the purposes of marriage (sukoon, lineage, mutual rights) are not achieved with a time limit; hence permanence (ta'bid) is a condition of the contract. Also, muwaqqat resembles mut'ah in meaning, and consideration is given to meanings.
The proof does not cite Quran or Sunnah explicitly; it is a qiyas based on the nature of marriage.
3
Understand Zufar's position and the Hanafi response
Zufar argues that the marriage is valid and the condition is void, since corrupt conditions do not invalidate contracts. The Hanafi response is that marriage is different; the time limit negates its essential objective.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the majority view.
4
Distinguish muwaqqat from mut'ah
Mut'ah uses the word tamattu' and requires mahr specification (like a sale), while muwaqqat uses the word nikah and does not require mahr. This distinction affects the legal category.
The difference is both in wording and in effect.
5
Note the exception from Abu Hanifa and the effect of intention
If the time limit is so long that the spouses would not normally live until its end, the marriage is valid because it is effectively perpetual. Also, if one marries unconditionally but intends a duration, the marriage is valid.
These exceptions show that the ruling hinges on the outward expression, not inner intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمؤقت : أي بطل النكاح المؤقت بأن تزوج المرأة مدة معينة ولو كان بشهادة الشهود، وقال زفر: يصح النكاح ويلزم، ويبطل اشتراط المدة؛ لأنه أتى بالنكاح والشرط، والنكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ولنا: أن مقاصد النكاح لا تحصل بالوقت، فكان من شرطه التأبيد، ولأنه متعة معنى والعبرة للمعاني والفرق في اللفظ؛ فإن المتعة يقع بلفظ التمتع، والمؤقت بلفظ النكاح، قيل: والفرق من حيث المعنى أيضاً وهو أن المتعة يشترط فيها تعيين مقدار المهر، فيصير بظاهره كالبيع، بخلاف المؤقت حيث لا يشترط فيه ذكر المهر ، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الزوجين إذا وقتا مدة لا يعيش مثلهما إليها صح النكاح؛ لأنه في معنى المؤبد، ولو تزوجهما مطلقاً وفي نيته أن يقصد معها مدة نواها فالنكاح صحيح، ولا بأس بتزوج النهاريات وهو أن يتزوجها على أن يقعد معها نهارا دون الليل، ولها أن ترجع وتطالبه بالمبيت عندها ليلا إن كان لها ضرة، ولا يمنعها الشرط السابق. (عيني، فتح) تتمة لم يتعرض المصنف لحكم النكاح المعلق بالشرط، فاعلم أن النكاح لا يصح إضافته إلى الزمان كما لا يجوز تعليقه بالشرط؛ لما فيه من معنى القمار كما لو قال لبنته إن دخلت الدار زوجتك من فلان، وقال: فلان تزوجتها فإن التعليق لا يصح وكذا النكاح. (فتح)
And al-muwaqqat: meaning the time-limited marriage is invalid, that he marries a woman for a specified time, even if witnessed. Zufar said: the marriage is valid and binding, and the condition of time is void, because he performed the marriage and the condition, and marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions. Our proof: the purposes of marriage are not achieved by a time limit, so perpetuity is a condition of it; and because it is mut'ah in meaning, and consideration is given to meanings, while the difference is in wording. For mut'ah occurs with the word 'tamattu' while muwaqqat occurs with the word 'nikah'. It is said the difference is also in meaning: mut'ah requires specification of mahr amount, making it like a sale, unlike muwaqqat which does not require mention of mahr. Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if the spouses set a time limit that they would not normally live until, the marriage is valid, because it is in the sense of perpetual. And if he marries absolutely but intends a specific duration, the marriage is valid. There is no harm in marrying 'al-nahariyyat' which is that he marries her on condition that he stays with her during the day and not the night. She has the right to retract and demand that he spend the night with her at night if she has a co-wife, and the prior condition does not prevent her. (Inayah, Fath) Supplement: The author did not address the ruling of conditional marriage. Know that marriage cannot be attached to time just as it cannot be suspended on a condition, because of the element of gambling. For example, if he says to his daughter: 'If you enter the house, I marry you to so-and-so,' and so-and-so says 'I marry her,' the suspension is not valid, and similarly the marriage. (Fath)
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage addresses muwaqqat (time-limited) marriage, which the Hanafi school declares invalid (batil) because marriage requires permanence (ta'bid). Imam Zufar differs within the Hanafi school, holding that the marriage is valid but the condition is void, arguing that corrupt conditions do not invalidate marriage. The Hanafi response is that the very essence of marriage contradicts a time limit; the purposes of marriage (sukoon, lineage, mutual rights) are not achieved temporally. The passage distinguishes muwaqqat from mut'ah: mut'ah uses the word 'tamattu' and requires mahr specification making it like a sale, while muwaqqat uses 'nikah' and may not specify mahr. A special case is narrated from Abu Hanifa: if the time limit is so long that they would not live to see it, it is valid as it is effectively perpetual. Also, if one marries absolutely but intends a duration, the marriage is valid. The 'al-nahariyyat' case (marrying a woman to be with her only during the day) is permissible, but the wife can later demand nighttime company. Finally, a supplement: conditional marriage (ta'liq) is invalid because it resembles gambling. Examples: 'If you enter the house, I marry you' – such conditional statements do not constitute a valid marriage.

Key Terms
النكاح المؤقت (al-nikah al-muwaqqat): A marriage contracted for a specified duration, e.g., for one year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is the ruling of a marriage contracted for a specific time (muwaqqat)?
A) Valid with a void condition
B) Completely invalid (batil)
C) Valid if witnessed
D) Valid only if mahr is specified

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a time-limited marriage is completely void because perpetuity is an essential condition of the marriage contract.

Nikah — Marriage

Nahariyyat Marriage and Conditional Marriage
Ruling statement on specific marriage conditions and principle on conditional marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on marrying a woman with a condition restricting nighttime company, and state why conditional marriage (ta'liq) is invalid.

Core Idea
Conditions restricting marital rights are not binding; marriage cannot be conditional on a future event due to gambling.

The second part of the passage addresses two practical issues: first, a marriage where the husband agrees to stay only during the day (nahariyyat), which is permissible but the condition is not enforceable. Second, the supplement clarifies that marriage cannot be made conditional (ta'liq) on a future event, as it resembles gambling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: nahariyyat marriage
The passage mentions 'tazawwuj al-nahariyyat' – marrying a woman on the condition that the husband stays with her only during the day and not at night.
This is a specific condition regarding the husband's company.
2
Note the ruling: it is permissible
The author says 'la ba'sa' meaning there is no harm; it is permissible (mubah).
The condition itself does not invalidate the marriage.
3
Understand the wife's right to retract
The wife can later retract her agreement to the condition and demand that the husband spend the night with her (if she has a co-wife). The prior condition does not prevent this demand.
This shows that such conditions are not binding; the wife has the right to equal division of nights.
4
Analyze the supplement: conditional marriage
The author notes that the main text did not cover conditional marriage (ta'liq). The ruling is that marriage cannot be attached to a future time (like muwaqqat) and also cannot be suspended on a condition (ta'liq).
The reason given is that it contains the element of gambling (qimar).
5
Examine the example of conditional marriage
The example: a father says to his daughter 'If you enter the house, I marry you to so-and-so,' and the man says 'I marry her.' The suspension is not valid, and consequently the marriage is not valid.
This illustrates that ta'liq in marriage is void.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

النكاح المعلق بالشرط (al-nikah al-mu'allaq bi al-shart): A marriage contract made conditional on a future event, e.g., 'If X happens, I marry you.'

Nikah — Marriage

Temporary Marriage (Nikah Mu'aqqat) Invalid
Ruling that a marriage limited to a fixed term is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on temporary marriage, explain the qiyas evidence, and distinguish it from analogous cases like mut'a and nahariyyat.

Core Idea
A marriage limited to a fixed term is invalid because perpetuity is essential to its validity.

The Hanafi school holds that a marriage contract with a fixed time limit (e.g., one year) is fundamentally invalid (batil), even if properly witnessed. This ruling is based on the purpose of marriage—companionship and lineage—which cannot be achieved under a deadline. In this lesson, we examine the proof, the objection from Imam Zufar, and the nuance of exceptionally long terms, as well as the distinct case of 'nahariyyat' marriage.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify that the default Hanafi position is: temporary marriage is invalid (batil) regardless of witnesses.
The text begins with 'والموقت : أي بطل النكاح المؤقت'.
2
Identify the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Note that Imam Zufar argued the marriage is valid and only the condition is void. Understand his reasoning: marriage is not invalidated by void conditions.
Zufar's view: 'يصح النكاح ويلزم، ويبطل اشتراط المدة'.
3
Follow the Hanafi Proof (Qiyas)
The proof uses qiyas to mut'a (pleasure marriage). Perpetuity is an implicit condition (shart) of marriage because its objectives require permanence. Temporariness contradicts these objectives, rendering the contract batil. Consideration is given to meaning, not wording.
The text: 'ولنا: أن مقاصد النكاح لا تحصل بالوقت، فكان من شرطه التأبيد، ولأنه متعة معنى والعبرة للمعاني'.
4
Analyze the Exception (Hasan's Narration)
If the period is so long that both parties would not survive to its end, the marriage is valid (as if perpetual). This shows the operative principle is the effective permanence of the term.
روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا وقتا مدة لا يعيش مثلهما إليها صح النكاح
5
Distinguish from Nahariyyat
A marriage where the husband stays only during the day is not a temporary marriage; it is a valid contract with a condition that the wife can later demand her right to night cohabitation. This clarifies that conditions that do not negate the essence are permissible.
نكاح النهاريات: يصح ولها أن تطالبه بالمبيت ليلا

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمؤقت : أي بطل النكاح المؤقت بأن تزوج المرأة مدة معينة ولو كان بشهادة الشهود، وقال زفر: يصح النكاح ويلزم، ويبطل اشتراط المدة؛ لأنه أتى بالنكاح والشرط، والنكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ولنا: أن مقاصد النكاح لا تحصل بالوقت، فكان من شرطه التأبيد، ولأنه متعة معنى والعبرة للمعاني والفرق في اللفظ؛ فإن المتعة يقع بلفظ التمتع، والمؤقت بلفظ النكاح، قيل: والفرق من حيث المعنى أيضاً وهو أن المتعة يشترط فيها تعيين مقدار المهر، فيصير بظاهره كالبيع، بخلاف المؤقت حيث لا يشترط فيه ذكر المهر ، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الزوجين إذا وقتا مدة لا يعيش مثلهما إليها صح النكاح؛ لأنه في معنى المؤبد، ولو تزوجهما مطلقاً وفي نيته أن يقصد معها مدة نواها فالنكاح صحيح، ولا بأس بتزوج النهاريات وهو أن يتزوجها على أن يقعد معها نهارا دون الليل، ولها أن ترجع وتطالبه بالمبيت عندها ليلا إن كان لها ضرة، ولا يمنعها الشرط السابق.
The temporary [marriage]: He said that the temporary marriage is invalid when a man marries a woman for a specific period, even if [the marriage] was with the testimony of witnesses. Zufar said: The marriage is valid and binding, and the condition of a period is void because he performed the marriage and [added] a condition, and marriage is not invalidated by void conditions. Our proof: The objectives of marriage are not achieved by a time limit, so perpetuity is a condition of it. And because it is mut'a (pleasure marriage) in meaning, and consideration is given to meanings, and there is a difference in wording: mut'a is concluded with the word tamattu', while the temporary [marriage] is with the word nikah. It is said: There is a difference in meaning too—mut'a requires specifying the amount of dower, so it appears like a sale, unlike a temporary marriage where mentioning the dower is not required. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: If the spouses set a period within which both are not expected to survive, the marriage is valid because it is in the meaning of perpetual. If he marries her absolutely but intends a specific period, the marriage is valid. There is no harm in marrying 'nahariyyat'—that he marries her on condition that he stays with her during the day but not the night—and she has the right to demand that he spend the night with her if she has a co-wife, and the prior condition does not prevent this.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof discussion about temporary marriage (nikah mu'aqqat), found in the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The main ruling is that a marriage limited to a fixed term is invalid, even if witnessed. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagreed, arguing that the marriage contract is valid and only the condition is void, since marriage is not invalidated by void conditions. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The purpose of marriage (companionship, children) is not achieved with a time limit, so perpetuity is inherent. (2) In meaning, it resembles mut'a (temporary pleasure marriage), which is prohibited, and consideration is given to meaning over wording. A further distinction is mentioned: mut'a requires specifying the dower, making it like a sale, while a temporary marriage does not. However, there is a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that if the period is so long that both parties would not live to see its end, the marriage is valid as it is effectively perpetual. Also, if a man marries absolutely but intends a term, the marriage is valid (the intention does not affect the contract). The text also discusses 'nahariyyat'—marriage where the husband stays only during the day—but this is not a temporary marriage; rather it is a condition that the wife can later demand her rights of cohabitation at night. This passage clarifies that temporary marriage is fundamentally invalid, but certain nuances exist regarding intention and extremely long terms.

Key Terms
النكاح المؤقت (al-nikah al-mu'aqqat): A marriage contract with a fixed time limit, which is invalid in the Hanafi school.
المتعة (al-mut'a): A temporary marriage contract for pleasure, explicitly prohibited and distinct from mu'aqqat in wording and ruling.
النهاريات (al-nahariyyat): A marriage where the husband agrees to stay only during the day, which is valid but the wife can later demand night cohabitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of a marriage contracted for a specific fixed term (e.g., one year) according to the majority Hanafi position?
A) The marriage is valid and the condition is void.
B) The marriage is invalid (batil) entirely.
C) The marriage is valid only if the period is very long.
D) The marriage is permissible if witnessed.

Key Takeaway
Temporary marriage is invalid in the Hanafi school because permanence is an essential condition; conditions contradicting the objectives of marriage void the contract.

Conditional Marriage Invalid
Ruling that conditional marriage is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a marriage contract cannot be conditioned on a future event and explain why it is invalid (batil) based on the analogy to gambling.

Core Idea
A marriage contract cannot be conditional on a future event — it is invalid because it resembles gambling.

This lesson clarifies a key principle in Hanafi marriage law: a marriage contract must be absolute and unconditional. The author explains that making a marriage contingent on a future condition or time renders it invalid, drawing an analogy to gambling due to uncertainty. Understanding this ruling helps you avoid invalid marriage contracts in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is a marriage contract made conditional upon a future event or time. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil).
The passage explicitly states 'the conditional is not valid, and similarly the marriage.'
2
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
The reason given is that it contains the meaning of gambling (qimar). This is because the occurrence of the condition is uncertain, introducing chance into a contract that requires certainty.
Gambling is prohibited in Islam; contracts with uncertainty resembling gambling are void.
3
Apply the example
The author gives an example: a father says to his daughter, 'If you enter the house, I will marry you to Zaid,' and Zaid says, 'I will marry her.' This arrangement is invalid.
The condition here is 'if you enter the house' — an uncertain future event.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies to any marriage contract that is made dependent on a future condition or added to a future time. The marriage must be immediate and unconditional.
This includes conditions like 'if I graduate' or 'if I get a job.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة لم يتعرض المصنف لحكم النكاح المعلق بالشرط، فاعلم أن النكاح لا يصح إضافته إلى الزمان كما لا يجوز تعليقه بالشرط؛ لما فيه من معنى القمار كما لو قال لبنته إن دخلت الدار زوجتك من فلان، وقال: فلان تزوجتها فإن التعليق لا يصح وكذا النكاح.
Supplementary: The author did not address the ruling of marriage made conditional upon a condition. Know that marriage cannot be validly added to a time [like the future] just as it is not allowed to be made conditional upon a condition, because it contains the meaning of gambling—as if he says to his daughter: 'If you enter the house, I will marry you to so-and-so,' and [the prospective husband] says: 'I will marry her'—then the conditional [promise] is not valid, and similarly the marriage.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This is a short supplementary note (tatimma) clarifying a missing ruling in the main text: conditional marriage (ta'liq). The ruling is that a marriage contract cannot be made dependent on a future condition, nor can it be added to a future time (like 'I marry you tomorrow'). The reason given is that it resembles gambling (qimar), because the occurrence of the condition is uncertain. The example: a father says to his daughter, 'If you enter the house, I will marry you to Zaid,' and Zaid says, 'I will marry her.' This arrangement is invalid. The same applies to any marriage contract that is conditioned on an uncertain event. This ruling is a straightforward prohibition; the nikah must be unconditional and immediate.

Key Terms
النكاح المعلق بالشرط (al-nikah al-mu'allaq bi al-shart): A marriage contract that is made conditional upon the occurrence of a future event, which is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the condition is permissible but the marriage is not.

Key Takeaway
A marriage contract must be unconditional and immediate; any condition based on a future uncertain event renders it invalid (batil) due to its resemblance to gambling.

Judge's Ruling with False Testimony in Marriage
Ruling on whether a man may sleep with a woman when judge ruled based on false witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's position that a judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective inwardly, apply the condition that the woman must be eligible for marriage, and distinguish this from absolute ownership claims.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling on apparent evidence is binding inwardly unless falsity is objectively detectable.

This passage addresses a critical scenario in Islamic judiciary: a woman claims marriage, presents witnesses, and the judge rules in her favor, but the man knows he never married her. The central question is whether the judge's ruling makes the marriage valid inwardly (before Allah), allowing the man to have intercourse. The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, holds that it does, while other Imams disagree. The passage also clarifies conditions and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and the first opinion of Abu Yusuf: the intercourse is permissible because the judge's ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly.
The man is certain he did not marry, but the judge's ruling overrides his personal knowledge.
2
Identify the opposing view
State the second opinion of Abu Yusuf, and the views of Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i: intercourse is not permissible because the judge erred due to false witnesses.
They analogize to cases where witnesses are found to be slaves or disbelievers.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand Abu Hanifa's dalil: the judge acted within his capacity; the witnesses appeared truthful; inner truth is unknowable; the judge is commanded to rule on apparent evidence.
The case of slaves/disbelievers is distinguishable because their status is objectively ascertainable through signs.
4
Note the condition
Identify that the woman must be eligible for marriage (not already married, not in 'idda, not thrice-divorced) for the ruling to take effect.
If she is ineligible, the judge's ruling does not take effect even outwardly.
5
Distinguish absolute ownership claims
Understand the consensus that in 'absolute claims' (al-amlak al-mursala), the judge's ruling does not take effect inwardly because the cause is unspecified.
This contrasts with marriage where the cause (the contract) is specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقضى بنكاحها: أي قضى القاضي بالنكاح بينهما . (ع) ولم يكن تزوجها : [ أي والحال أن الرجل لم يكن. (ع)] أي إذا ادعت امرأة على رجل أنه تزوجها فجحد الرجل ثم أتت بشاهدين فشهدا عليه أنه تزوجها، فقضى القاضي بشهادتهما عليه، والحال أن الرجل متيقن أنه لم يتزوجها، قيل: حل له وطيها عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في القول الأول، وقال أبو يوسف في الآخر وهو قول محمد والشافعي: لا يحل له وطيها؛ لأن القاضي أخطأ الحجة؛ إذ الشهود كاذبون فصار كما إذا ظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفار، وله أنه قضى بما في وسعه، والشهود صادقون عنده لا عند الله تعالى؛ لأن الوقوف على حقيقة الصدق متعذر لا يعلمها إلا الله تعالى، والقاضي مأمور بالقضاء بالشهادة الصادقة عنده، بخلاف ما إذا وجدا كفاراً حيث لا ينفذ القضاء؛ لأن الوقوف على هذه الأشياء متيسر بالأمارات، أما هنا فقد بالغ في التفحص عن حال الشهود فلم يوجد منه تقصير. والشرط أن تكون المرأة محلاً لإنشاء النكاح حتى لو كانت ذات زوج أو في عدة غيره أو مطلقة ثلاثاً لا ينفذ قضاؤه، ومسألة المتن هي . مسألة قضاء القاضي بشهادة الزور فينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً عند أبي حنيفة، والمراد من النفاذ ظاهراً ثبوت حكمه كالتمكين والنفقة والقسم وغير ذلك، والمراد من النفاذ باطناً ثبوت الملك، والحل فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى، وأن إثم المدعي بإقدامه على الدعوى الكاذبة، ولا خلاف بينهم في الأملاك المرسلة أن قضاءه لا ينفذ، ومعنى المرسلة أن يدعي الملك المطلق، ولم يذكر له سبباً بأن قال: هذا ملكي وأقام البينة عليه، وقضى به القاضي، فقضاؤه لا ينفذ؛ لأن في الأسباب كثرة، وليس بعضها أولى من بعض حتى لو ذكر سبباً معيناً، فإن كان يمكن إثباته من جهة القاضي إنشاء مثل البيع والإجارة كان على الخلاف، وإن كان لا يمكن كالإرث لا ينفذ قضاؤه اتفاقاً.
He said: 'And the judge ruled in her favor regarding the marriage': That is, the judge ruled that the marriage [is valid] between them. 'And he had not married her': That is, while the man had not [actually married] her. That is, when a woman claims against a man that he married her, and the man denies, then she brings two witnesses who testify that he married her, and the judge rules based on their testimony, while the man is certain he did not marry her. It is said: It is permissible for him to have intercourse with her according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the first opinion. Abu Yusuf in the other opinion, which is the view of Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, said: It is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her because the judge erred in the evidence, as the witnesses are liars, so it becomes like when they appear to be slaves or disbelievers. His [Abu Hanifa’s] proof: The judge ruled based on what was within his capacity, and the witnesses are truthful in his view, not in Allah’s view, because ascertaining the reality of truth is impossible—only Allah knows it. The judge is commanded to rule based on testimony that appears truthful to him. This is unlike when they are found to be disbelievers, where the ruling does not take effect because ascertaining such matters is possible through signs. Here, the judge made a thorough investigation into the witnesses' condition and no negligence was found. The condition [for validity] is that the woman be eligible for marriage; if she is already married, or in the ‘idda of another, or thrice-divorced, his ruling does not take effect. The issue of the text is: the judge's ruling based on false testimony takes effect outwardly and inwardly according to Abu Hanifa. 'Outwardly' means the implementation of the ruling like enabling [cohabitation], maintenance, division, etc. 'Inwardly' means the establishment of ownership and permissibility between him and Allah, and the sin is upon the plaintiff for proceeding with the false claim. There is no disagreement among them regarding absolute claims of ownership (al-amlak al-mursala) that the judge's ruling does not take effect. Meaning of mursala: he claims absolute ownership without mentioning a cause, like saying 'This is mine' and presents evidence, and the judge rules accordingly—his ruling does not take effect because there are many possible causes and none is more likely. Even if he specifies a cause, if it can be established through the judge's own creation like sale or lease, there is difference of opinion; if it cannot be established like inheritance, the ruling does not take effect by consensus.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific mas'ala: a woman claims marriage, brings two witnesses, and the judge rules in her favor, but the man knows he never married her. The ruling on whether he may have intercourse differs. According to Abu Hanifa and the first opinion of Abu Yusuf, it is permissible for him to have intercourse because the judge's ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly. The reasoning: the judge did his best and the witnesses appeared truthful to him; since absolute truth of testimony is unknowable except to Allah, the ruling is binding. Abu Yusuf's second opinion and the view of Imam Muhammad and Shafi'i say it is not permissible because the witnesses are lying, so the judge erred. The passage then clarifies a condition: the woman must be eligible for marriage; if she is married or in ‘idda, the ruling does not take effect. It also contrasts with cases of 'absolute claims' (al-amlak al-mursala) where the judge's ruling does not take effect inwardly by consensus. The key takeaway: Abu Hanifa holds the judge's ruling based on apparent truth is effective inwardly, even if the witnesses are lying, unless there is clear evidence of their disqualification (like being slaves or disbelievers).

Key Terms
نفاذ القضاء ظاهراً وباطناً (nafadh al-qada' zahiran wa batinan): The judge's ruling is effective both in external legal consequences (cohabitation, maintenance, etc.) and in the spiritual/moral realm before Allah, making the marriage valid inwardly.
الأملاك المرسلة (al-amlak al-mursala): Absolute claims of ownership without specifying a cause, where the judge's ruling does not take effect inwardly by consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The witnesses must be male and Muslim.
B) The woman must be eligible for marriage (not already married, not in 'idda, not thrice-divorced).
C) The man must admit the marriage.
D) The judge must have personal knowledge of the case.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view is that a judge's ruling based on apparent evidence is binding inwardly, but with conditions: the woman must be eligible, and the judge must have conducted proper investigation; absolute ownership claims are an exception.

Marriage Without Guardian: Hanafi Position and Proofs
Ruling that a free adult woman may contract her own marriage without a guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage without a guardian and evaluate the opposing proof using the Hanafi dalil and critique of 'Aisha's hadith.

Core Idea
A free adult woman's marriage is valid without a guardian — the Hanafi school rejects the supposed hadith requiring one.

One of the most debated issues in Islamic marriage law is whether a woman needs a guardian (wali) to contract her marriage. The Hanafi school stands out among the four major schools by allowing a free adult woman to marry herself without a guardian's involvement. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position, its internal variations, and the proofs that support it against the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali objection.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the core ruling: marriage of a free adult woman without a guardian is valid and binding according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (final view).
The term 'free and legally capable' (hurra mukallafa) is key.
2
Identify the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools cite the hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian and two just witnesses.' Recognize this as their main dalil.
This hadith is narrated by some companions.
3
Analyse the Hanafi counter-proof
Examine the Hanafi dalil: the authentic hadith 'The formerly-married woman is more entitled to herself than her guardian' and Quranic verses (2:230, 2:232) that attribute marriage to women.
Bukhari and Ibn Ma'in are cited to deny any authentic hadith requiring a guardian.
4
Evaluate the critique of 'Aisha's hadith
Understand why the Hanafis reject 'Aisha's narration (Any woman who marries without guardian, her marriage is invalid): because she acted contrary to it by marrying her niece while her brother was absent.
Hanafi usul: a narrator acting against their own narration invalidates it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify the operative ruling for fatwa: Abu Hanifa's view that the marriage is valid without guardian, with which Abu Yusuf eventually agreed. Muhammad's suspended view is not relied upon.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأولياء والأكفاء أي في بيان أحكامهم ... نفذ نكاح حرّة مكلّفة بلا ولي ... أي إن زوجت حرة مكلفة نفسها بغير شهود ولي وإذنه نفذ نكاحها عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في ظاهر الرواية، وكان أبو يوسف يقول أولاً: إنه لا ينعقد إلا بولي إذا كان لها ولي ثم رجع، وقال: إن كان الزوج كفواً لها جاز، وإلا فلا، ثم رجع وقال: جاز سواء كان الزوج كفواً لها أو لم يكن. وعند محمد: ينعقد موقوفاً على إجازة الولي سواء كان الزوج كفواً أو لم يكن، ويروى رجوعه إلى قولهما، وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد: لا ينعقد بعبارة النساء أصلاً؛ لقوله عليه: "لا نكاح إلا بولي وشاهدي عدل". ولنا قوله علية: "الأيم أحق بنفسها من وليها" متفق على صحته، وما رواه لم يصح. وكذا كل ما روي في هذا الباب؛ ولهذا قال البخاري وابن معين: لم يصح في اشتراط الولي حديث، ولنا أيضاً قوله تعالى: ﴿ حَتَّى تَنْكِحَ زَوْجاً غَيْرَهُ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٠) وقوله: ﴿وَأَنْ يَنْكِحْنَ أَزْوَاجَهُنَّ (البقرة: ۲۳۲) أضاف العقد إليهن فدل على أنها تملك المباشرة بالنكاح. وأما حديث عائشة هما: "أيما امرأة نكحت بغير إذن وليها فنكاحها باطل"، الحديث فلا يعمل به؛ لأنها عملت بخلاف روايتها حيث زوجت بنت أخيها عبد الرحمن وهو غائب، والراوي إذا عمل بخلاف ما روى تبطل روايته.
Chapter of Guardians and Compatibility, i.e., explaining their rulings. ... The marriage of a free, legally-capable woman [is valid] without a guardian ... That is, if a free, adult woman marries herself without a guardian's presence or permission, her marriage is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the apparent narration. Abu Yusuf initially said it is not concluded except with a guardian if she has one, then retracted and said if the husband is suitable it is valid, otherwise not, then retracted again and said it is valid regardless of suitability. According to Muhammad, it is concluded contingent upon the guardian's permission, whether the husband is suitable or not, and it is narrated that he retracted to their view. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said it is not concluded by women's words at all, based on the hadith: 'No marriage except with a guardian and two just witnesses.' Our proof: The hadith: 'A formerly-married woman has more right to herself than her guardian'—agreed upon as authentic; what he narrated is not authentic. Also everything narrated in this chapter is unsound; hence Bukhari and Ibn Ma'in said no authentic hadith exists for the requirement of a guardian. Also the verse: 'Until she marries another husband' (2:230) and 'And that they marry their husbands' (2:232)—He attributed the contract to them, indicating that they possess the capacity to directly perform the marriage. As for the hadith of 'Aisha: 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid'—it is not acted upon because she acted contrary to her own narration when she married the daughter of her brother 'Abd al-Rahman while he was absent, and when a narrator acts contrary to his narration, his narration is invalidated.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on guardians (awliya') and compatibility (kafa'a). The core ruling is that a free adult woman (hurra mukallafa) may contract her own marriage without a guardian, and it is valid and binding according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the apparent opinion. The passage traces the evolution of Abu Yusuf's view: he initially required a guardian, then conditioned suitability, then finally agreed with Abu Hanifa. Imam Muhammad holds that the marriage is suspended on the guardian's approval. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools hold that women cannot contract marriage at all; a guardian is absolutely required, citing a hadith. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: (1) The hadith 'The formerly-married woman is more entitled to herself than her guardian' is authentic, and no authentic hadith requires a guardian (as stated by Bukhari and Ibn Ma'in). (2) Quranic verses attribute the marriage action to the women themselves (e.g., 'until she marries' and 'that they marry their husbands'), indicating women have the capacity to execute the contract. The hadith of 'Aisha is rejected because 'Aisha herself acted contrary to it—she married her niece without the guardian's presence—so it is invalid according to Hanafi usul. This passage clearly establishes the Hanafi position that a woman's self-marriage is valid, with details on internal Hanafi differences.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The guardian in marriage, defined as the 'asaba (agnate relative) who has authority to contract the marriage of a minor or, in other schools, of an adult woman.
الأيم (al-ayyim): A woman who has been previously married (not a virgin), but in context refers to any adult woman who is free to marry (including divorced or widowed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the hadith of 'Aisha that states 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid'?
A) Because the hadith is not authentic according to Bukhari and Ibn Ma'in.
B) Because 'Aisha acted contrary to her own narration when she married her niece without the guardian present.
C) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran.
D) Because it is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a free adult woman to contract her own marriage without a guardian, relying on authentic hadith and Quranic verses, and rejecting the opposing hadith as unauthentic.

No Compulsion of Adult Virgin in Marriage
Ruling that a guardian cannot compel an adult virgin to marry against her will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compelling an adult virgin into marriage and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the evidence provided.

Core Idea
Adulthood terminates guardianship of compulsion; a guardian cannot force an adult virgin to marry.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a fundamental disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: may a father compel his adult virgin daughter to marry? The text clarifies the Hanafi position that compulsion (ijbar) is based on minority, not virginity, and provides the proof from hadith and legal reasoning. Understanding this dispute helps you appreciate how the Hanafi school prioritizes the legal capacity of an adult woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of guardianship
Notice that the text distinguishes between wilayat al-nadb (advisory) and wilayat al-ijbar (compulsory). Determine the basis for each according to the Hanafi school.
Compulsory guardianship applies only to minors, insane, and enslaved persons.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The passage explicitly states that an adult virgin (bikr baligha) cannot be forced into marriage. This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is categorical: 'لا تجبر'.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a guardian may compel an adult virgin because virginity implies inexperience, analogous to a minor. Identify the qiyas used by the Shafi'i.
The opposing proof is analogy (qiyas) to a minor.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on (1) a direct hadith that the virgin must be asked for consent, and (2) the principle that adulthood confers full legal capacity. Note how the Hanafi response addresses the Shafi'i analogy.
The hadith is explicit: 'al-bikr yusta'dhanuha abuha'.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Shafi'i, the father can marry his adult virgin daughter without her explicit consent; under Hanafi, her consent is required, and silence or laughter implies consent, not coercion.
This difference affects the validity of the marriage contract.

ولا تجبر: اعلم أن الولاية على نوعين ولاية ندب وهي الولاية على العاقلة البالغة بكراً كانت أو ثيباً، وولاية إجبار: وهي الولاية على الصغيرة بكراً كانت أو ثيباً، وكذا الكبيرة المعتوهة والمرقوقة، فمدار الإجبار عندنا على الصغر، فمعنى قوله لا تجبر بكر بالغة أي لا يجوز للولي إجبار البكر البالغة على النكاح، وقال الشافعي: له إجبارها؛ لأن مدار الإجبار عنده على البكارة اعتباراً بالصغيرة؛ لأنها جاهلة بأمر النكاح؛ لعدم التجربة، ولنا: أنها حرة مكلفة، فلا يكون الغير عليها دراية، وقال عليه : "البكر يستأذنها أبوها"، رواه مسلم والولاية على الصغيرة؛ لقصور عقلها، وهنا قد كمل بالبلوغ بدليل توجه الخطاب إليها والتصرف في مالها . على النكاح ولو كان المزوج أبا أو جداً. الولي الأقرب بأن قال: أريد أن أنكحك فلاناً.
And she (the adult virgin) is not forced: Know that guardianship is of two types: Guardianship of suggestion (wilayat nadb) which is guardianship over an adult sane woman, whether virgin or non-virgin; and guardianship of compulsion (wilayat ijbar) which is guardianship over a minor, whether virgin or non-virgin, and similarly over an adult insane or enslaved woman. So the basis of compulsion with us is minority. Thus the meaning of his statement 'An adult virgin is not forced' is that it is not permissible for a guardian to compel an adult virgin into marriage. Al-Shafi'i said: He may compel her because the basis of compulsion with him is virginity, by analogy with a minor, since she is ignorant of marital affairs due to lack of experience. Our proof: She is a free adult, so no one has authority over her. The Prophet said: 'The (consent of the) virgin is sought by her father'—narrated by Muslim. Guardianship over a minor is due to her deficient intellect. Here she has reached perfection by adulthood, evidenced by direct address (taklif) and her ability to dispose of her property.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that an adult virgin (al-bikr al-baligha) cannot be forced into marriage by her guardian. It begins by distinguishing two types of guardianship: (1) Wilayat al-nadb (advisory guardianship) over an adult sane woman, where the guardian merely advises. (2) Wilayat al-ijbar (compulsory guardianship) over a minor, and similarly over an insane or enslaved woman. The key difference is that compulsion is based on minority, not virginity. Imam Shafi'i held that a guardian can compel an adult virgin because he considers virginity as the basis, comparing her to a minor who lacks experience. The Hanafi response: adulthood confers full legal capacity (mukallafa), so no one has authority over her. The Prophet hadith ('al-bikr yusta'dhanuha abuha') indicates that even the father must seek her permission, implying she cannot be forced. The passage also notes that the guardian cannot force her even if he is the father or grandfather. The practical outcome: the guardian must seek the virgin's consent; if she stays silent or laughs, that is considered consent, but she cannot be coerced.

Key Terms
ولاية الإجبار (wilayat al-ijbar): Guardianship of compulsion, applicable only to minors and incompetent adults, allowing the guardian to contract marriage without the ward's consent.
البكر البالغة (al-bikr al-baligha): An adult woman who has never been married; she has full legal capacity and cannot be coerced into marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The guardian being the father.

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi law, an adult virgin cannot be forced into marriage; compulsion is reserved only for minors and those lacking legal capacity.

Prohibition of Forcing a Virgin Adult in Marriage
Explaining the prohibition of forcing a virgin and her consent methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a virgin adult cannot be forced into marriage and explain why the basis of compulsion is minority, not virginity.

Core Idea
A virgin adult cannot be forced – compulsion in marriage is based on minority, not virginity.

This lesson examines the Hanafi prohibition of compelling a virgin adult (bikr balighah) into marriage. The text distinguishes guardianship of recommendation (wilayat nadb) from guardianship of compulsion (wilayat ijbar), asserting that only minors and the insane can be forced. We will explore the proof from the hadith and the Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i position, which allows forcing a virgin due to alleged inexperience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
The text states 'a virgin adult is not to be forced' (لا تجبر بكر بالغة). Compulsion (ijbar) is prohibited. The basis of ijbar is minority (sighar) and insanity, not virginity. Confirm this distinction from the text.
Note: The ruling is specifically for a virgin who is adult (balighah).
2
Examine the Two Types of Guardianship
The text describes wilayat nadb (guardianship of recommendation) for sane adults, and wilayat ijbar (compulsion) for minors and the insane. Understand that a virgin adult falls under wilayat nadb, so she cannot be forced.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i Counter-Argument
Al-Shafi'i analogizes the adult virgin to a minor, claiming she lacks experience. Identify his qiyas and the basis of his position (virginity, not minority).
Shafi'i considers the virgin's inexperience as a reason for guardians to have compulsion.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Proof and Response
The Hanafi response: she is free (hurrah) and legally responsible (mukallafah). The hadith 'The virgin – her father seeks her permission' (البكر يستأذنها أبوها) is cited. Explain how this hadith proves prohibition of compulsion and establishes that permission must be sought.
The hadith is from Muslim; its threat is direct command to seek permission.
5
Note the Authority and Fatwa Position
The text indicates that the fatwa is on the view that silent crying is not rejection, but the overall mufta bihi position is that the virgin adult cannot be forced. The cross-madhhab dispute is noted: Hanafi prohibits, Shafi'i allows compulsion.

فهو إذن [ أي كل واحد مما ذكر من السكوت والضحك والبكاء. (ط، ع)] أما السكوت؛ فلقوله عليه: "لا تنكح الثيب حتى تستأمر، ولا تنكح البكر حتى تستأذن، قالوا: وكيف إذنها يا رسول الله؟ قال: "تسكت"، رواه مسلم، وأما الضحك فرضاء دلالة؛ لأنه علامة السرور والفرح بما سمعت وكذا إذا تبسمت، وقيل: إذا ضحكت كالمستهزئة بما سمعت لا يكون رضاً، بخلاف ما إذا بكت، فإنه دليل السخط والكراهة، وقيل: إذا بكت بلا صوت لم يكن رداً، بل حزناً على مفارقة أهلها، وعليه الفتوى، وقيل: إن كان دمعها بارداً يكون رضا، وإن كان حاراً لا يكون رضا، ويعتبر في الاستيمار تسمية الزوج على وجه يقع لها به المعرفة؛ لتظهر رغبتها فيه أو إعراضها عنه، ولا يشترط ذكر المهر في الصحيح ثم إنه سوي بين الاستئذان وبين بلوغ الخبر بالتزويج؛ لأن وجه الدلالة في السكوت لا يختلف بين أن يكون قبل العقد أو بعده، ثم المخبر إن كان ولياً فعن أبي يوسف: أن سكوتها بعد العقد يكون ردا وهو قول محمد وعند أبي حنيفة يكون رضا ورسول الولى كالولي، ولو كان المخبر فضولياً . يشترط فيه العدد والعدالة عند أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لهما. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٠/١] غير الولي: أي الولي الأبعد مع وجود الأقرب. (ط) من القول ولا يكون سكوتها رضا؛ لأن سكوتها لقلة الالتفات إلى كلامهم فلا يدل على الرضا. (ط ، ع)
And a virgin adult (balighah) is not to be forced into marriage. If the guardian seeks her permission, and she keeps silent, or laughs, or cries, or he marries her and the news reaches her and she remains silent without being scornful, without sound — that is (the guardian acting) without seeking her permission after the marriage, i.e. the news of the marriage, i.e. the virgin adult. And know that guardianship is of two types: guardianship of recommendation (wilayat nadb), which is the guardianship over the sane adult, whether virgin or thayyib; and guardianship of compulsion (wilayat ijbar), which is the guardianship over the minor, whether virgin or thayyib, and likewise the adult insane and the slave. So the basis of compulsion with us is minority. Thus the meaning of his saying 'Do not force a virgin adult' is that it is not permissible for the guardian to force the virgin adult into marriage. Al-Shafi'i said: He has the right to force her, because the basis of compulsion with him is virginity, by analogy with the minor, since she is ignorant of the matter of marriage due to lack of experience. Our proof: she is free and legally responsible, so another cannot have authority over her. And the Prophet ﷺ said: 'The virgin — her father seeks her permission,' narrated by Muslim. And guardianship over the minor is due to her deficient intellect, but here she has become complete by adulthood, as evidenced by the address of obligations to her and her right to dispose of her property. (Ayni, Mustakhlas, Fath) ... So it is permission (idhn). And if someone other than the guardian seeks her permission, then speech is necessary, like the thayyib. (Then the commentary explains: ) So it is permission, i.e. each of the mentioned (silence, laughter, crying). As for silence, due to his ﷺ saying: 'Do not marry the thayyib until she is consulted, and do not marry the virgin until her permission is sought.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, how is her permission?' He said: 'By her silence,' narrated by Muslim. As for laughter, it is indicative consent because it is a sign of joy and happiness at what she heard, and likewise if she smiles. It is said: if she laughs scornfully at what she heard, it is not consent. Unlike if she cries, for that is a sign of displeasure and dislike. It is said: if she cries without sound, it is not rejection but sadness at leaving her family, and upon this is the fatwa. It is said: if her tears are cold, it is consent; if hot, it is not consent. In consultation, it is required to name the husband in a way that she recognizes him, so that her desire or aversion appears. Mention of the dowry is not required in the correct view. Then it is made equal between seeking permission and the arrival of the news of the marriage, because the indication in silence does not differ whether it is before or after the contract. Then, if the informer is a guardian, according to Abu Yusuf: her silence after the contract is rejection, and that is the statement of Muhammad. According to Abu Hanifa, it is consent. And the messenger of the guardian is like the guardian. If the informer is a non-relative (fuduli), then the conditions of number and uprightness (adalah) are required according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (the two). (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 200/1) 'Other than the guardian': i.e. the distant guardian when the nearer is present. (T) By speech, and her silence is not consent, because her silence is due to lack of attention to their words, so it does not indicate consent. (T, A)
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage addresses two interrelated rulings: (1) a virgin adult cannot be coerced into marriage, and (2) the methods of consent for a virgin differ from those for a non-virgin. The text opens by stating that a virgin adult (bikr balighah) is not to be forced (la tujbir). It then distinguishes between two types of guardianship: wilayat nadb (guardianship of recommendation, i.e., over sane adults) and wilayat ijbar (guardianship of compulsion, i.e., over minors, insane, and slaves). The key principle: compulsion is based on minority, not virginity. Al-Shafi'i is mentioned as opposing this, arguing that a virgin can be forced due to her inexperience; the Hanafi response is that she is legally responsible (mukallafah), so no one can compel her. The hadith 'The virgin – her father seeks her permission' (Muslim) is cited to support this. The second part discusses how consent is indicated. If the guardian asks permission, the virgin's silence, laughter, or crying without sound indicate consent, while explicit speech is not required for the virgin. For the thayyib (non-virgin), explicit speech is necessary. The commentary elaborates on the nuances of each reaction, including the distinction between laughing scornfully (not consent) and crying silently (considered sadness, not rejection). The fatwa is that crying without sound is not rejection. It also discusses the scenario when the news of an already-conducted marriage reaches the woman: if the informer is the guardian, silence after the fact is considered consent according to Abu Hanifa, but rejection according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. If the informer is a non-relative (fuduli), strict conditions of number and uprightness are required per Abu Hanifa. Finally, if someone other than the guardian (e.g., a distant relative) seeks permission, then speech is required for consent, and silence is not sufficient because the woman may not pay attention to them. This passage is from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq commentary and falls under the authority of the mutakhkhirin, relying on the primary texts.

Key Terms
إجبار (ijbar): Compulsion; a guardian's right to force a person into marriage against their will. In the Hanafi school, this applies only to minors and the insane.
بكر (bikr): A virgin; a woman who has never had sexual intercourse. In this context, a virgin whose hymen is intact.
ثيب (thayyib): A non-virgin; a woman who has had sexual intercourse. Her consent must be expressed explicitly in speech.
فضولي (fuduli): A non-relative informer; a person who is not the woman's guardian and reports the marriage to her. Strict conditions apply for her silence to be valid as consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The virgin's inexperience
B) The hadith that the virgin's permission must be sought
C) The principle of ijbar based on minority, not virginity
D) The Quranic verse on women's rights

Key Takeaway
A virgin adult cannot be forced into marriage; compulsion is invalid because it is based on minority, not virginity.

Consent of a Virgin: Silence, Laughter, and Crying
Explaining the prohibition of forcing a virgin and her consent methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid signs of a virgin's consent (silence, laughter, crying without sound) and distinguish between different informer scenarios (guardian vs fuduli) that affect whether silence indicates consent.

Core Idea
A virgin's consent is shown by silence, laughter, or silent crying – but only when the informer is the guardian.

This lesson focuses on the specific methods by which a virgin indicates her consent (idhn) in marriage. Unlike a non-virgin (thayyib) who must speak explicitly, a virgin may show acceptance through silence, laughter, or crying without sound. We will analyze each of these signs, the fatwa that silent crying is not rejection, and the crucial distinction of who informs her: the guardian or a fuduli (non-relative). The text also covers an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether silence after being told of an already-conducted marriage counts as consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Signs of Consent
The text lists: silence (sukut), laughter (dahk), and crying (buka) without sound. Each is a form of permission (idhn) for a virgin. Confirm from the hadith about silence and the commentary on laughter and crying.
Note: The thayyib requires explicit speech (qawl).
2
Understand the Reasoning for Each Sign
Silence: based on the hadith 'her permission is her silence.' Laughter: a sign of joy and consent. Crying without sound: sadness at leaving family, not rejection. Examine the fiqh rulings and the fatwa that silent crying is not a rejection.
3
Compare Before and After Contract
The text equates seeking permission before the contract and informing after the contract. The same signs apply. Understand that silence after being informed of an already-concluded marriage is treated like permission before.
4
Distinguish the Informer's Identity
If the informer is the guardian (wali), silence is consent per Abu Hanifa (but rejection per the two). If the informer is a fuduli, strict conditions (number, uprightness) are required per Abu Hanifa, and even then, silence is not considered consent if the informer is not the guardian. If someone other than the guardian (e.g., distant relative) asks permission, speech is required.
Note: The fuduli must be multiple and upright according to Abu Hanifa.
